RATING: 8
Another fantastic game by Fantasy Flight.  Although it is very competitive and offers an array of expansions in the form of various ships.  The game is split into three factions: Rebels, Imperials, and Scum and Villany.  Each faction has their pros and cons.  My main faction for this game is the S&V faction, flying the Firespray (Slave I).  You can outfit your ships with a variety of different cards, although, some cards might not be available in expansions for your particular faction.  So you will need to buy an expansion even though you can't use the ship in your fleet.  Otherwise a great game.

You FEEL like you're in an X-Wing or TIE fighter, swooshing around in space, blasting your opponent. The components are excellent, the miniatures look BEAUTIFUL, the rules are simple, straightforward, well-explained, and well-realized, and the game just works! If you're a Star Wars fan, this is a definite buy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I played this game just once, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

I'm not a fan of miniature games. I tried a couple but I always found them too long, too expensive and too boring because of all the dice rolling. X-Wing kinda surprised me instead.

The biggest strength of this system is its simplicity. It's quite easy to play and you don't have to rely on convoluted charts or long calculations to determine hits and damages. This leaves a lot of space for tactical and strategical decisions. The second biggest strength of the game is its strong theme. The movement in particular feels very "realistic" and gives you the feel of piloting a spaceship quite a bit.

On the other hand, I'm still not that big a fan... but it's merely for personal tastes. I recognize the merits of this title, but it's still a bit too long for me and it has too much dice rolling. Also the personalization of your army didn't excite me as much as I expected. Maybe with additional plays in the future my opinion might change.

To sum up: Good system, easy to understand and very thematic. Still not my cup of tea.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
FAVOURITE GAME - An excellent tactical ship-to-ship combat game based on the Star Wars universe. You either choose to play with the Rebel Alliance or the Galactic Empire. The gameplay is quite easy: you secretly plan you moves and then execute them together with any special actions available. The combat is more or less a question of luck, as you roll dice, although having some option to modify the results. The starter set does not confer an epic feel to the game, but if you choose to upgrade your fleet by buying units it becomes awesome.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Slick. 

Everything about this is a promise fulfilled in terms of the big-company, big-license game. Finally FFG gets the little things right: the rules are finally at-standard, the fans get their 'realism' and the game doesn't drown in superfluous components. 

The game is just fun, fun, fun. It's accessible (which Wings of War is not, strangely). It's fast (not only a 20-30 minute game, but turns move fast). It's got enough skill and granularity to keep you interested. 

Unfortunately, I gave up on it when it seemed like you needed a tonne of ships and playspace to make the to-and-fro interesting. If you want a customisable minis game, I think this is worth it, but if you want an affordable board game, might be too much $$$.

RATING: 8
Great looking miniatures. Simple rules, fast paced gameplay. I am afraid that the core set is not enough to fully appreciate the game. I also find unacceptable that the core set doesn't come with enough dice. Come on FFG! 

Επιτραπέζιο παιχνίδι με μινιατούρες από την Fantasy Flight Games στο στυλ του κλασσικού Wings of War. Αρχικά να πω πως οι μινιατούρες είναι prepainted και φαίνεται να είναι καλής ποιότητας και πιστά αντίγραφα των σκαφών αν και δεν είμαι ειδικός επί του θέματος. 

Οι κανόνες είναι πολύ απλοί και λειτουργικοί. Ο κάθε παίκτης διαλέγει ταυτόχρονα και κρυφά τι κίνηση θέλει να κάνει το κάθε σκάφος του. Μετά με την σειρά το κάθε σκάφος κινείτε χρησιμοποιώντας το αντίστοιχο template (ξεχάστε hexes και μεζούρες) και επιλέγει ένα action. Αφού κινηθούν όλα τα σκάφη μετά αρχίζει η μάχη και ρίχνουμε τα ζάρια. 

Στο ταμπλό μπορούμε να τοποθετήσουμε και μετεωρίτες για εμπόδια, ενώ τα σκάφη είναι κάπως παραμετροποιήσημα αφού μπορούμε να επιλέξουμε τον εξοπλισμό που θα φέρουν. Σκοπός είναι να καταρρίψεις όλα τα αντίπαλα σκάφη αλλά υπάρχουν στους κανόνες και 2-3 σενάρια με διαφορετικά objectives.

Μου άρεσε που το παιχνίδι έχει γρήγορο ρυθμό και καταφέρνει να σου περάσει την αίσθηση του να πιλοτάρεις ένα σκάφος. Είναι πολύ διασκεδαστικό και αν έχεις περισσότερα σκάφη τότε μπορείς εύκολα να παίξεις και με περισσότερους από 2 παίκτες. Το μόνο αρνητικό είναι πως το βασικό σετ είναι περισσότερο σαν demo του πραγματικού παιχνιδιού. Για να φτιάξεις ένα πραγματικό στόλο χρειάζεται να πάρεις 2-3 ακόμα σκάφη. Παράλληλα θα ανοίξουν και οι επιλογές από κάρτες εξοπλισμού.

Όμορφο, απλό, γρήγορο, και εθιστικό. Δεν ξέρω όμως πόσες παρτίδες θα σας βγάλει το βασικό σετ προτού χρειαστείτε το κάτι παραπάνω.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
I finally succumbed to X-Wing at about the time the Imperial Aces were released. Foolishly, I bought the core set for my brother’s birthday and we played it together. Then we played it again. Then again. And then again.

There have been few games in recent memory that have had such an immediately positive impact on me. It’s so simple; it’s so neat and logical; it’s so fun and thematic. There and then at the table we each agreed to sink a silly amount of money into buying more of these expensive little plastic ships.

That said, I don’t feel that X-Wing is offensively overpriced either. I’ve often been put off many other miniature games I’d probably love by the prohibitively expensive costs of starting the hobby. But here I don't feel ripped off when I pay around £11 or 12 for an "expansion pack".

X Wing also gets plus points from me because I detest painting models – and I think these ships are far nicer looking than the Star Trek (and now D&D Attack Wing) stuff from WizKids.

The ridiculous part of all this is that I’m not actually a very big Star Wars fan – though it might always have been the rabid, lunatic fans that put me off the franchise rather than the films themselves.

Anyway, in short, this game is insane. Stay the hell away from it if you have disposable income you’d like to keep in your pockets.

One noticeable downside is that it can actually take quite a bit of effort to get it on the table and playing when you have plenty of different ships if you don't invest in decent ways to organise your X-wing gear.

RATING: 9
No other game I can think of has so such a high ratio of thematic depth to mechanic complexity, and no other table-top miniatures game can fit (core set, rules, multiples of each expansion) into a single small tackle box.  Some may decry the miniature price (about $15 for each fighter), but I would argue that those that complain, either don't care about the aesthetics of their game, or don't value their time (it would take me at least an hour to assemble, prime, paint, and seal a ship to the above-average quality at which these miniatures come out of the box).  I wouldn't say it is the best gaming experience in any one area (tactical depth, theme, aesthetics, etc.), but if all these categories were combined into a boardgame decathlon then X-Wing would be best overall game by finishing in the top-5 in several areas.

RATING: 8
Set aside nostalgia for a moment.  If this were a game about generic combat in space, would it be any good?  The surprising answer is yes.  The core mechanisms in the game are derived / lifted / borrowed from Wings of Glory.  Each ship has maneuvers that can be selected and a movement template that shows where the mini should end up.  The physical aspects of moving the ships is well thought out and works very well for the target audience (likely younger gamers).  And that's where you might think the game ends, but not so.  X-Wing combines a squad building and customization element into the game.  It is this customization and the rules framework (150 pt squads, 3' x 3' play area, etc) that really make this minis game shine.  When you add in the fact that you are playing with iconic star ships, you have a winner.  A solid and containable minis game that works well.  And that nostalgia... its not so bad either.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
X-Wing is an average game made good (maybe even very good) by it's outstanding production.  At its core it's a guessing game as players try to out maneuver their opponents on the table top.  Each side decides what all their ships will do simultaneously -- if you are clever/lucky and predict correctly you'll likely wind up in a better firing position than your opponent.

As in so many collectible games, a big part of the enjoyment will be customizing your squadrons.  Matching this ship with that pilot and those upgrades, trying to synergize special abilities and find killer combos is a big part of the game -- at least in "serious play"

The game plays simple and usually ends pretty quickly.  So much so that it's almost in the realm of a filler.

One downside is that its cost.  The base set isn't too bad but only enough miniatures to whet your appetite.  A proper introduction to the game probably requires at least another 2-4 ships (about 50 dollars more). If you DO decide to jump in and pick up lots minis, you'll also need to figure out a storage solution (something Im not quite sure I've accomplished yet). 

Also - with any game where dice have a major effect on the outcome, you can get some games that end abruptly, and others that overstay their welcome (as your fighters limply misfire at each other over and over again).

Ultimately the quality of the pre-painted miniatures and the very real sense of a swooping, spinning, star wars dog fighting make this game an enjoyable diversion if your willing to fork over the cash. 

(2 core sets)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Neat idea.  Heavily luck reliant.  The game just did not have staying power to keep my interest.

A bevezető játék után egy óvatos pontszámot adok a játéknak, de látom benne a fantáziát: a teljes játék akár sokkal jobb is lehet. Már a legegyszerűbb szinten (bevezető szabályok, 3 hajó) is jó kis taktikai játék, ahol azért szerencse is van rendesen: attól, hogy ügyesen manőverezek és sikerül ráfordulnom az ellenséges hajóra, úgy hogy az nem is tud visszalőni, még egyáltalán nem biztos, hogy el is találom. RATING: 8
Excellent game, a lot of fun and excellent replay-ability. Reasonably high investment if you play in tournaments, meta-bloat due to design issues frequently invoke many in the community to declare that the game is "pay-to-win". Fantasy Flight is also blamed to some degree of not fully play testing expansions before their release, thereby creating such problems as a result. Despite these 'niggles', casual and Epic play is superb, mission play and the ability to create your own scenarios makes this game one of the most popular pre-painted miniatures titles.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.1
This is a great system to play with miniatures. It seems almost everyone loves it.

I can't give it a perfect score though as it still is a collectable game which means its active life span to acquire extra miniatures is limited in time.

The majority of these games only last 3 years or so on a personal basis and after that you are stuck with lots of plastics/cards and an empty pocket. eg Dragon Dice - almost any LCG/CCG outside Magic - A&A miniatures...

This game seems to last longer and the Star Wars craze may put it into a higher orbit.

There is also an extreme good web based App for solo play and that is awesome because solo play extends every game's life cycle as you don't depend on finding other players for an older game.

So I would recommend a buy but I would also suggest: limit your purchases to 5 or 6 miniatures per side to keep control on your expenses.

Be warned. It is an extremely tense and competitive game and you WILL get caught by the "I need MORE XWing fever".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
This is a great game set in the Star Wars Universe, which makes many ships recognisable to the fans. It combines (i) deck building like in a trading card game/ living card game, (ii) nice pre-painted models, (iii) simultaneous action selection and (iv) dice.
Since many interesting lists are only composed of two ships it´s also relatively cheap to start playing the game (you "need" some upgrades from different ship expansions though if you want to take it a little more serious). 
One of the most interesting aspects is the simultaneous action selection. You have to think what the other player will do while they do the same. So there is some room for surprises and a lot of skill involved in flying the ships effectively. 
Although this is a dice game and luck plays a role, the ability to outmaneuvre your opponent is more important. Some upgrade cards also let you modify your dice results.

I would recommend it to casual as well as more competitive players. The latter will probably get even more out of it (thriving meta game in store, regional and world championships).

RATING: 6.5
Well, I told myself that I wouldn't get into another minis game because of the money pit, but I succumbed when I finally saw the game and ships in action. Coming from a minis background, I don't find the price point that expensive as expressed by others. The miniatures are painted and assembled; so that's a big plus for me. 

This is a mostly a tactical game where squad building and maneuvering plays a major part of succeeding on the board. Yes, there could be some randomness with the dice, but it could also be mitigated with the different abilities of the pilots and ships. Squad building can be fun, but I suggest one of the many squad builder's out there to make it simpler and quicker. This is the one I am using at the moment which has printable armies to boot:

http://xwing-builder.co.uk/build

What is great about the game is the way that the theme is captured with the gameplay and beautiful ships. Even though I am not a diehard fanboy of Star Wars, I found myself getting into the theme. I even watched the movies afterwards. Anyways, you will find yourself making pew pew sounds when you are involved in a battle and if you're not doing them out loud, then you are thinking about it.

Great stuff! Highly recommended; especially for dads and sons/daughters.

RATING: 7
I was eager to play X-Wing, as I read so many praises about it: luckily, a friend of mine was even more eager than I and recently bought this game with as many expansions as he could lay his hands on. We immediately started playing it, so I discovered all those praises weren’t undeserved: X-Wing is decidedly a fine game.

Undoubtedly it reminds Wings of War but this similitude is only superficial: actually, by getting rid of the dedicated card decks and streamlining most manoeuvers, X-Wing improves Wing of War’s gameplay and makes it both easier and deeper, making for many more tactical options and unpredictability than the latter.

I can’t help but think the Rebels have slight advantages over the imperial fleet: they're not game-changing but relevant enough to force the Empire player to avoid any mistake. [i](August 2013)[/i]

[b]Update[/b] - I’m so fed up with this Star Wars frenzy which seems to have infected everyone lately that now I can barely stand anything linked to this annoying saga: moreover, playing X-Wing has become so bulky and time-consuming that I’m glad to avoid it for the time being.

Hence, I lowered my rating from 9 to 7 in December 2015.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
I've been agonizing all day trying to put my finger on what it is about X-Wing Miniatures that stops me from considering it one of my favourite games, because on paper its got it all.

Tiny, beautiful minis set in the Star Wars universe, battling it out for galactic supremacy... what's not to love?

There's amazing theme, wonderful aesthetics, heavy tactics and a smattering of luck, all in seemingly near-perfect balance, so why don't I LOVE this game?

And I'm sorry to disappoint, but I'm still not sure.

All I can say is that I've never walked away from a game thinking "well, that was excellent"... even if I've won. 

I think perhaps that every game I've played has gotten very predictable, very quickly, with not a great deal of movement and action variation (certainly in the core set). 

Sure, tactics are hugely important, but it seems to me to be a lot of micro management and I don't think there's enough scope for some 'big moves' that have the potential to upset the balance of power.

Maybe I'm wrong - perhaps its just fundamentally not my kind of game, but I reeeeally want it to be.

The agonizing continues......

RATING: N/A
Only played this game solo so far and am enjoying the theme very much.  Its definitely a light game.  Not much in the way of realism, in that I mean if you are following another ship, you should be able to follow it and make your heading changes according to what he does.  Instead you have to both secretly choose a maneuver and hope you guessed right, if not then for some odd reason he turned left and you turn right then so be it.  If you can deal with situations like that and like Star Wars I think you will like this game.  It is really fun, the ships look amazing and it plays pretty fast.  The rules are very light as well.  Another negative is the way this game is marketed.  If you get hooked your wallet will take a pounding by buying new ships at about $15 each, it adds up pretty quickly.  FFG definitely knows what they are doing.

RATING: 7
The pluses are obviously it's Star Wars and beautifully done right out of the box. Pretty easy rules that get a little complicated with multiple upgrades for each ship. The minus is plodding game play and fiddliness. Like all real-life-based fighter combat games, which I love, with several ships a side to make a decent battle, each turn takes several minutes so it's hard to keep the connection between lightning fast movie combat that we see on the screen and the glacial pace of this game. Add in the inevitable furball with ships' placement and movement, and template alignment- what a mess. Have to try the Hex version of this! All the gripes aside, the pluses outweigh the minuses if the fights are kept to a reasonable size, and upgrades are limited to a few per ship.

RATING: 8
-sold-

Since the game got worn out it hit the table less and less. So I decided to sell the whole fleet.

---

Great skirmish game. I love it. I own 2.
The planning mechanic where you set your maneuvers in the dial and you have to plan ahead with "I think you are going there so I should going here and you might be expecting that so I do something different."
Plus you have a squad-building aspect with a strong interaction between the ships, the pilots and the equipment. I really love it.
Quickly explained and it's a cheap variant of a tabletop game (as long as you play it casually with just the base set and maye a handfull of expansions).

...well well well...
After time passed by I reconsidered my rating. It still is a great skirmish-style game that can totally be recommended but for me it has lost it's shine. I still like it but it is not a game that I still wish to play as often as possible. Maybe it's time to let it rest a bit...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Massive improvement over the core mechanics from Wings of War. The addition of a movement DIAL (instead of cards) alone is an outstanding change. Plus the ship customization and Action system add much better strategic and tactical depth.

The game still suffers from a few old Wings of War problems though. Moving through other units still requires estimation of the final location. Also, the ships can wiggle a bit while attempting to move them. A felt play surface could help reduce this. I also don't like the official "rule disagreements" resolution system of rolling dice.

RATING: 7
BGG says I'm up to 11 plays; pretty sure it's substantially more than that.

This is a game I play and always enjoy, but I'm going to again express my mixed feelings about the whole thing, especially the most recent sets. Even though, again, I do enjoy it.

As they dig deeper into the EU, X-Wing does feel like it's selling cool toys, and not really a game. With the constant pinging around of the metagame with each new wave, and scenarios that are a really mixed bag, the play experience gets a bit uneven. I've actually found the epic ships - the CR90 and particularly the most recent Imperial Corvette - to be the most frustrating, with very sketchy scenarios and campaign systems and somewhat questionable playability on the ships themselves. They look absolutely great on the table. I just don't know if they play that well, except for the Rebel Transport which works fine just as a moving target for scenario objectives.

Anyway, the game is Star Wars, and it's good enough. But like everything from FFG, it's not hard to wish the i's had been fully dotted, and the t's crossed. Both Wings and Sails of Glory are much better games, but they aren't Star Wars :)

---

Been playing this a bit more recently, which has been fun. It's cool just to get the nice minis out on a nice playmat and mix it up. For infrequent play, though, one thing I find a bit frustrating is just how lucky the game is. Recently I was playing the Preystalker scenario, where the Imperials try to jump a single target ship. The scenario starts with the target at a severe positional disadvantage, with the Imperials able to unload one full round of fire without the Rebels able to do much about it. I decided I needed to dispose of at least one of the escorts first, before they could really return fire, before tackling the main target (the Millennium Falcon). The hail of blaster fire from the initial salvo did exactly nothing, and that essentially decided the game. The Rebels turned around, I was outgunned, and that was that. Because of the really swingy nature of the combat system, if the dice are fickle games can turn pretty quickly on the first kill unless your squad is really robust. Anyway, I still enjoy the game, but especially now - with so many ships and so many combos available, with such a complex meta-game and with so many unbalanced cards - it's a hard game to play if you're not seriously into it enough to be able to quickly prune the game space.
---
Mixed feelings. Lacks the grace and elegance of Wings of War, and there isn't as much interesting nuance to the tactics of X-Wing as there is to either WWI or WWII Wings of War, and X-Wing's damage system is very swingy. On the other hand, X-Wing does have cool squadron-building and pilot abilities, and it plays fast. On balance, fun, but I seriously doubt it has the staying power of its sister game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I've never played a miniatures game before, but the combination my love of Star Wars and the focus on accessibility convinced me to give this a try, much like many other people I'm sure.

I'm sure this isn't unique to THIS game in particular, but there's something that feels cool and freeing about moving around a huge play space rather than a grid on a board. Everything about this game evokes the feel of a real space battle.

The minis themselves are lovely. I justified my purchase of the game just by telling myself that even if I hate the game, at least I'll have cool Star Wars toys.

I've only played with the base set so far and, fair warning, it's really, really not enough. It feels like playing the introduction to a system and not at all a full game. If you're looking for a game that is fun and replayable out of the box you're pretty out of luck here.

So let's see here: plus-points for: accessibility, pacing, length, bitchin' minis, variety of ships (in that they all feel different), and options for building your fleet. So what's on the negative side?

Disclaimer: Some of this is due to the makeup of the starter ships.

...but the luck factor is just too high. The system in place to mitigate the luck is the Action mechanic. The idea is, if you choose your actions smartly (based on what you think your opponent will do) you will be able to increase your odds of attacking or evading.

However, with the starter fleet any increase you can get your opponent can easily match, thus making it come down to just... pure luck. It's too easy for BOTH sides to easily roll the same number of dice (or close to it) and have the same perks (rerolling dice or changing their values.) Perhaps it was a mistake to allow Focus to have the same effect for defense as it does for offense.

There are moments where this game feels like a fun mind game of bluff and double-bluff, but because combat is so lackluster that's really ALL there is to the game (and really, there are better psychological games around). I'm sure this game is more fun with a greater variety of ships as the metagame of building your fleet becomes ever more important, but as it is the game feels just too shallow for me to want to really invest in.

So... mindless and expensive? Under what circumstances would I ever recommend this? Well, I believe games have an emotional component. And this evokes the Star Wars theme like basically nothing else... so if you want to spend half an hour indulging in the fantasy of piloting an X-Wing then this will do you.

RATING: 10
The game is massively expensive (at least $140 MSRP to have a decent 100v100 fight), it relies a bit too much on luck (dice based combat), and is very fiddly (measuring templates, hundreds of chits, tons of upgrade cards modifying rules with rerolls, etc.)

That said, this is Star Wars dogfighting at its finest.  There is nothing more satisfying than completing the perfect maneuver that skirts the edge of an asteroid and brings your opponent straight into your crosshairs for the kill shot.

On top of that, the models from FFG are absolutely top notch.  The paint jobs, the attention to detail, and the iconic designs make the models themselves worth the cost of admission.  The fact that FFG provides rules for a fun, exciting game for which to use these models is almost gravy.

RATING: 9.5
Ok went to GENCON and had a blast this year. So last year I tried out the playtest version of this and was not impressed at the least. So I was not inclined to try it this year figuring that FF didnt listen to the suggestions. We ll went by and my buddy decided to get a box set and a few blisters. I decided to give it a second chance and I have to say that they have a winner in this game. The pieces are slick and well made. The ships are sweet and the rules are very well put together. We played a couple more demos and by the end of the day the two of us were in for 6 box sets and about a dozen blisters of the X-wing, TIE fighter, TIE advanced and Y wing. We went back to the hotel and popped open the game with a couple of other gamers we met and went about doing a 150 pt game with each getting 75 pts. we were quickly in to a good fight and the dice gods were on my side by the end of it. I decided to go with 2 xwings and lots of add ons and the rest went with a couple of big guys and a lot of little guys. it plays smooth, has enough diversity between the two factions and the sides balance well. I recommend this game very highly and you should give it a shot. BTW on Saturday after 3pm they slipped models of the Millennium Falcon, Slave 1, A Wing and the TIE interceptor into the display case with a release date of winter 2012. The blisters come with extra counters and more pilot and upgrade cards so you should get them as well. 
Later and hope this helps,

RATING: 9.75
This game captures some of the excitement I felt when I first saw X-Wings and Tie Fighters battle in the original movies over two decades ago.  But even if I wasn't a Star Wars fan, I would still have to appreciate the detailed models, strategy, and refreshing game mechanics that make this game shine.  The different ships and cards give great variation to squadron building and especially clever is that both players must secretly select ship movement (done by using a dial that is placed face down).  All of this creates a brilliant sense of anticipation and enjoyment as you wait to see if you correctly predicted your opponent’s next move in order to line them up in your firing arc.

RATING: 7
My first and only miniatures game.  I love the theme, the mechanics, and mostly the customization of forces.  Very reminiscent of the old TIE fighter video game, which was one of my all time favorite video games.

For me, the meat of the game is how to trick out your forces using the upgrade cards.  I would be bored silly playing with the 8 tie academy swarm, since they can't take their upgrades.  I also tend to enjoy the decision tree regarding movement.  There is a bit of the she thinks I will go here, but I will go here, but maybe that is what she is expecting because she thinks I won't go there doublethink that keeps movement selection interesting.

I am partial to smaller battles.  The wife tends to pick a build she likes, and that is my point target for the game.  It seems like you can balance the core set and wave 1 to favor a particular side based on points allowed.

I am certainly not into this for the tournament scene.  Since I love the customization so much, I think playing the same squad for multiple games (which I am pretty sure I have not yet done) would bore me. I like to sit back, pop in a CD of the soundtracks and take my new squad out for a spin each time we play.

Na veel onderzoek online te hebben verricht naar een toegankelijke wargame kwam star wars x-wing bovenaan uit de lijst rollen. Volledig nieuw in dit genre storten ik en een paar vrienden, die zelfs amper bordspellen spelen zich op deze game. Iedere aanwezige is lierisch over het spel. De miniaturen zijn van groot detail voor mij als leek is de paint job super.( vermoedelijk discutabel voor de pro printers ;-) ). De meegeleverde schepen ogen fragiel dus neem voorzichtigheid in acht! De meegeleverde tokens en kaarten zijn van goede kwaliteit, voor de kaarten heb ik zelf plastic hoesjes aangeschaft. Als je allereerst de 3 meegeleverde missies speelt wordt geleidelijk de game uitgelegd, langzaam besef je dat het spel doormiddel van upgrades aardig te diepte in kan duiken. De spelregels zijn goed te begrijpen mits je engels kan lezen. Binnen 10 min heb je het spel aan een medespeler uitgelegd en spelenderwijs na 1 avond onder de knie. Bij mij werd na avond 1 direct geopperd een vaste gameavond in te plannen. Met de basis set ben je waarschijnlijk een paar keer zoet en omdat je zelf missies kan samenstellen blijft het leuk maar ik merk dat hoe meer units je op tafel brengt de epische veldslagen nog beter tot zijn recht komen. 1 min puntje Is dat de basis zet maar 3 dobbelstenen van elk bezit, dit terwijl je een enkele keer een 4de nodig hebt. Ik heb 2x de basissen aangeschaft. Dit is verre weg het efficiënts. ( indien je toch wil upgraden ) Voor mijn persoonlijk een dikke 10. ( leeftijd aanwezige 25 - 30 )

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Well thought out mechanics, especially the simultaneous turns. Players are faced with tough and meaningful tactical and strategic decision making during game-play, as well as during the squad and equipment selection process. Strikes a good balance between customization and streamlined list building. Overall game balance is fairly good - most equipment and ship options are useful, and it's entirely possible to build semi-competitive squadrons that adhere to the fluff.

The main negative point is the relatively high amount of random chance. The maneuvering aspect is totally player-determined, but combat is dice based (and quite deadly and unforgiving). There are many dice-manipulation mechanics that players can exploitt, but relatively few dice are rolled over the course of the game, which results in a lot of variance in combat results. Despite this, the game rewards skillful play enough that skilled players can consistently defeat weaker players.

Update Dec 2016, 270 plays: Bumped the score up to 10. Continues to be one of the most interesting competitive two-player game I've played. The current competitive metagame is very rich, but relies overmuch on ability combos instead of maneuvering.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Great fun and really doesn't take much time to learn!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Rating for the entire game [family=18113]family[/family]. This deviates from my usual policy to rate base games and expansions separately, but I think the X-Wing base games just can't sensibly be rated without their expansions. They obviously weren't designed to be played with just a base game.
My rating contains a sizeable bonus for the existence of a large official, well-organized tournament scene, the fact that the official FAQ is updated regularly and that FFG is not afraid to change cards that turn out to be too weak or particularly too strong.
I would like the game considerably better if movement and check for viable targets were based on hexes (or squares) instead of the fiddly and imprecise maneuver templates and a line laser.
Moreover, expansions are published too frequently for my taste: The meta changes too quickly and it is too expensive to stay competitive.

RATING: 3
Miniatures games have never been my cup of tea, and this game reminds me why:  (1) fiddly measurement/movement; and (2) a protracted set-up phase where you try to build your army within the point limit.  

All this planning and attention to detail becomes downright silly with paired with the game's central mechanic:  chucking dice.  Plus movement is rather chaotic, and it's often a matter of pure guesswork whether your move is the right one.

The miniatures are well made, but honestly, who (other than 11-year olds) cares?  If that's important to you (and you have $100 to spend), then you'll love this puerile dice-fest.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I love everything about this game. 

It's incredibly easy to get into, there are a handful of rules in the base game and the movement templates take all of the usual hassle associated with movement in miniatures games out of this. Add to this a very high quality tutorial video from FFG (which is amazing, more of this please board game makers in general!) and rather than the usual one or two games to get into the rules it only took one or two rounds.

The game itself plays fast and is good fun. The miniatures all look fantastic, a little pricey but given the quality, and the fact that it saves me having to hand paint everything, it seems like a price that's worth paying (especially when compared to how much you need to spend on the average miniatures game to field a force).

Given it a 9 rather than a 10 because I'm not too sure about longevity. The next few waves of ships look great and are must-haves, beyond that they will be getting into obscure ships that don't have the same appeal, at which point you will be largely fighting the same dogfights over and over. The best way around this would be more scenarios and a full campaign ruleset, if they make that wave 4 then this has the legs to run for a long time.

RATING: 10
(two base sets, multiples of each expansion)

My initial ranking of this game is more a reflection of how often I would want to get it to the table than a declaration of its true objective value if measured in some kind of vacuum (like outer space! har har). Huh...not sure that made sense.

I love the game, so much so that I've bought enough of the expansions to stay competitive even though I know I'm not going to play it at, say, GenCon. 

But it's involved to set it up and put away (and I'm a hypocrite about that because I don't mind the effort with Heroscape). It's also a lot of brainpower if you're flying enough ships, but not in a complex way as much as a taxing/exhausting way. 

I avoided it at first because it wasn't Wings of War. And I was wrong for doing so. No, it's not WoW/WoG, instead it's yet another form of skirmish combat with miniatures. But we're talking the king of themes here and it works; if you don't feel like you're in the middle of an epic Star Wars space battle, that's your fault, not the game's.

Update: Increasing rating to a 9. In many ways, X-Wing is a combination of Wings of War and Heroscape, two of my favorite games of all time.

Okay, fine...my original 7 rating was too low, obviously (not sure what I was thinking). It sets a bit of a challenging hurdle to initially overcome (for the reasons stated above, and flying well is still not easy). But it's such a great game! Each Wave release has been well thought out without any obvious "feature creep", at least through Wave 3. And anything that produces a gigantic Transport and Corvette should be rewarded!

So I still don't get to play this anywhere near enough, but I managed to win a local store tournament and had a blast doing so, even if afterwards I felt like I had a migraine.

And now I'm upgrading it to a 10. It's everything I love in a game: Dice, board positioning (flying), sometimes simultaneous selection (allows for outguessing), and most importantly, the game outside the game, where you can always make tweaks here and there. Heroscape will always be my first love, but this is a close second.

RATING: N/A
Played the intro rules a couple of times with my 7-year-old. This is basically Wings of War, but plotting one move at a time instead of three and using a little maneuver-select dial per ship with shared cardboard movement templates instead of individual maneuver decks. This speeds up play a little bit, leaving room for chrome. The pilot cards, upgrades, and action system are ingeniously simple while adding all kinds of flavor.

Not rating officially until I play the full game with adults, but my kid and I had a blast playing the intro game (and he wants to try the full rules next). Unless my initial impressions are sorely mistaken, I expect to award this game a 9 at least.

RATING: 6

The miniatures are pretty cool, though, and it definitely works well for large groups.

RATING: 5
This game (especially the core box) felt incomplete to me. The mechanisms seemed good, the theme is beloved, and yet the game just didn't strike that chord.

I feel that this may in part be due to the components included in the core box. The base game comes with 2 Tie Fighters and 1 X-wing (along with all the tokens/cards/rulers needed to play). This was serviceable enough, but the dogfights felt shallow. We purchased a second core box to add some more ships to each players arsenal... and still the game felt unfulfilling. Then we purchased some different ship expansions like the Millennium Falcon and the Slave 1 to add some variety... and still the game felt unfulfilling. At this point, it was hard not to draw comparisons to games like MTG or Warhammer where it would take an endless stream of money and expansions to make the game feel whole.

Maybe the game would feel better if the gameplay wasn't focused around the point-based skirmishes (ALA Warhammer 40k) and had more of a story or campaign like its ground based cousin Imperial Assault. Ultimately, the game just felt more like a constant treadmill of buying expansions to shape that perfect fleet rather than a good game in and of itself.

A pity, I really wanted to like it too.

RATING: 7
I'm always shocked when FFG puts together a playable game, but I'll admit that the bar is getting raised. 

X-Wing is pretty much a carbon-copy of the great Wings of War card game. But they sped up the game with longer distance moves and only one phase of programming. 

The changes are great thematic ones: lock-ons, proton torpedoes, a simple shield mechanic, and a robust pilot-skill for initiative. He might be standing on eth shoulders of giants, but I give a lot of credit to the great development work by Jason Little, kudos!

RATING: 9
One of my new favorite games to come out in the last few years.  It reminds me of HeroScape. The game play isn't similar, but you get to pick out cool miniatures, and they have special abilities (different pilots and Upgrade cards). You build a squad based on point values, there are easy movement rules, and the combat with rolls for attack and defense is easy but fun.

The other thing about HeroScape it reminds me of is after you set up a game, you want to play a few more times because the setup and take-down is longer than an individual game. 

My son loves the game, and would probably love to play every day if he could.

It is a fun game to play 1 vs. 1, but is also a good convention game. I think playing a massive battle on huge tables at a convention would be a great experience.

RATING: 10
At this point I think I'm ready to claim that XWing is the best of the Flight Path Games and better than Wings of Glory (but for different reasons). The game is tight, well designed, atmospheric and tense. Everything from production to editing and quality control is top shelf. It is just a great and competitive game. I've come to love the clear and separate factions that are balanced (Looking at you Star Trek) and love that the same level of component quality has remained constant (glace back at Star Trek). Also, the scaling of three different ship sizes is an amazing accomplishment and how it all works. My only gripe is that scenario play is really non-existent. Sure there's some here or there, but the default mode of a handful of asteroids and 100 pts became the default because it creates a tense game, but a samey game.

RATING: 8
This may have been an obsession of mine if it wasn't for Android Netrunner taking up too much real estate in my brain. 
   The game is fun from the very first time you move a ship along a template, inducing the inevitable "neeeyowww" sound that all kids make when playing with toys. Movement and combat is fundamentally simple, made insanely deeper by the vast array of ship cards, pilot cards and upgrade cards in the game. FFG have done the Star Wars IP justice and created a beast of a competitive game. 
    However, matches do tend to end with little drama, with both players drawing the game to a usually inevitable conclusion as the single remaining ship is chased down over one too many turns. 
    Nethertheless, I'm usually up for a game and often find myself looking at my grossly under-used collection with a tinge of guilt.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.8
I'm not real big on minis games.  The imprecision of it bugs me too much.  No matter how careful you are when you put the ruler in front of your ship and move it, it can slide a couple millimeters.  Pieces can be bumped, firing arcs can be ambiguous, and you never know when one of these minuscule errors is going to alter the outcome of a game.  Now, I'm nowhere near OCD enough that this is going to stop me from playing, but still.

X-wing in general is pretty well-designed.  The point-buy system is relatively simple: select a ship, pick which 'level' you want (how skilled a pilot is going to be flying it), match the icons at the bottom of the card to any add-ons you want to include, and repeat for the other ships.  The game plays quickly and smoothy: set orders for your ships, then each one moves, does an action, and shoots in turn order.  They've done a great job keeping it customizable yet simple.

My only gripes are that I think some granularity's been lost along the way.  The ships roll 1-3 attack and evade dice, and have some mix of shields and hull points, as well as a list of maneuvers they can perform.  This means that as far as the game's concerned, a lot of the ships have very similar (or the same) stats.  An A-wing is the same firepower & maneuverability as a TIE fighter, as a TIE advanced, and an an E-wing is the same as a TIE interceptor, as a TIE defender.  Likewise, a B-wing is exactly as tough as a Y-wing, an E-wing the same as a TIE advanced, a λ shuttle as a YT-2400 freighter, etc.  When you're choosing between such small numerical ranges, you're going to get a lot of ships that feel awfully similar, differentiated only by special abilities and equipment load-outs.  There are some of these things that just [i]feel[/i] wrong, especially if you've played the video games.  A TIE phantom is no more maneuverable than the bomber?  A Y-wing no more than the shuttle?  The Millennium Falcon's shields are no stronger than a B-wing's?  These sorts of flavor quibbles are pretty minor, though.
What really frustrates me is the way the game handles (or fails to) the 3-D nature of a dogfight.  I'm fine with the fact that this is all played out in 2-D on a tabletop.  Not having differing 'heights' for the ships is additional complexity probably best left out.  However, the actual rules are way too restrictive, imo.  If you ever try to do a maneuver that you can't complete due to another model being in the way, you have to cut your move short, you lose your action, and you can't shoot at the ship in front of you.  That last part is fine; if you're assumed to be flying above/below the other ship, so you wouldn't have a clear shot at it.  But the fact that you can be penalized so heavily (basically losing your turn) for an action that should be completely normal in a dogfight (diverting a little above or below a passing ship) really irritates me.  You can't even declare your intent to do this if you think someone's going to get in your way.  All you can do is try and outguess them, which might not even be possible depending on the number of ships near you.  Oh, and I think it's nonsense that the ships going later in turn order (with ostensibly the greater piloting skill) are the ones more susceptible to this.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
So, initially I was turned off to this game because there were only three star fighters included in the Core set. The game was completely off my radar when I happened upon the rules on FFG's website. I read through the rules and was very impressed by the simplicity. I decided to try a demo of the game while I was at Gen Con and I was very impressed with the game play. I ended up buying two Core sets and one each of the first expansions. The rules are easy to understand and explain. The minis are great looking in my opinion, and game play is fun. I was able to play this game with my 16 and 11 year old children and they had no issues comprehending the rules. If you're thinking about trying this game, give it a shot. I don't think you'll be disappointed. I wasn't.

RATING: 7.65
This game acted solely as a toy collection for a very long time until finally another friend of mine both his first pack. From then on we got hooked. It is indeed extremely good game of miniature space battles. Hidden movement selection is beautiful mechanic. Design is almost flawless. The biggest complain are somewhat clunky ship overlapping rules due to the lack of 3rd dimension. It's 2D space battle game with beautiful, lovely well known star wars space craft models. 
It's good 1 on 1, it's good with 3, 4, even 5 players. Scenario based, free for all or just plain skirmish, I don't see the point where we get tired of it.

Not perfect score because of the price (core set is not enough), money drain and above mentioned overlapping clunkiness.

[b]Update:[/b] Long setup and transportation issues when collection grew bigger caused me to lower the rating from 9 to 8.
[b]Update:[/b] Rating modified according to a custom rating system.

[b]Favorite mechanism:[/b] Secret simultaneous movement dial allocation for every ship is ingenious. It speeds up the game and it's making it intense and unpredictable.

RATING: 8
Full Squadron Building and Customization. Low Cost Tabletop Quality Pre-painted Miniatures. Easy to Learn Rules but Deep Strategy. Superb Suspense with Hidden Movement Dials. Fast Gameplay (1-1.5 hr for most common game size). Captures the Feel of being in a dogfight.

A Masterpiece in Game Design, but flawed in execution in terms of balance and replayability. The lack of standard scenarios (as compared to Armada for example) significantly affect replayability and limit loadouts. In terms of balance, FFG hasn't yet mastered balancing various abilities as they are released and usually relies on the next wave, months away, to balance current imbalances that they could easily balance with immediate erratas.

RATING: 8
I love Star Wars, but I don't love all things Star Wars (see: Episodes I - III and the ridiculous number of poor computer translations, etc.) I have only rarely played miniatures games. I really enjoy SW:XW Miniatures and obviously it's partly due to the theme. It feels like your in a dogfight from the movies. But it's also a really well-designed game. Your favorite iconic characters are right there in the game and have interesting abilities to make them play a bit differently from the generic pilots of the same ships. Much of the strategy actually happens before the game begins during Squad Building. Fantasy Flight has designed endless combos of pilots and capabilities that you can try out on the playfield (at least, if you acquire a few expansion ships). The actual gameplay can get pretty chaotic due to hidden moves and difficulty you'll sometime have in lining up a shot. I imagine that a real-world dog fight has a similar feel however. I recommend 2 core sets both to have more TIEs and another X-Wing, but also b/c you'll double the number of dice on hand which frequently comes in handy. FF should have included several more of each die.

RATING: 5

My FLGS is working on a deathstar trench run for its first tournament which is cool.

Scenario one seems very heavily slanted in favour of the rebels.
Scenario two seems heavily slanted in favour of the empire, as does scenario three.

Tie fighters are really hard to hit if they keep trying to evade and therefore its difficult to stop them if they have a mission that is not destroy.

I am a little dissappointed in the TIE fighter and X-wing packs as of the 6 "new" pilots and  4 "new" pilots  3 and 2 (half!) are the same as the base game pilots

A-wings are fast and fragile as they should be and man Y-wings can take some hits. The ion cannon seems disgustingly overpowered as it is an action to shoot it not a shoot, therefore you can effectively fire twice.
 
Millenium Falcon was won at the local Kessel run event :)

Imperial Aces purchased as surprise gift for b/f ;)

Whilst I am luke-warm on this game the B/f loves it and so has all the ships, many in multiple. Rather than try to keep up with the collection I will list it under just the base game.

Sold the complete collection in 2016.

RATING: 10
After the Star Wars LCG left a very bad taste in my mouth, I wasn't sure X-Wing was going to be great. Happily, my hesitation was totally wrong - I love this game. It has occurred to me that the best way to play Star Wars is doing exactly that - going out in the backyard and having lightsaber duels or flying around plastic ships and blowing up your friend's plastic ships. The latter is, of course, exactly what this game is, taking the fun of playing with Star Wars toys and providing a standardized rule set, and it's a blast. The ships are so varied by now (Wave 6 is out, Wave 7 coming very soon) that getting into the game at this advanced stage is wonderful - I have one of everything, two of many things, and three or more of a few faves; so many that there is a lot of depth to building interesting fleets from game to game. This is gonna be tons of fun for a long time.

Games have had a good tension and no 'system killer' loopholes have appeared and the possibilities of new skills, ships, weapon cababilities and even maneuvers means that the game should stay fresh throughout it's life.

RATING: 9
X-Wing is a great miniatures game.  The ships are so awesomely detailed and the components are supreme all the way. Beyond that, the mechanics keep things simple but there is just enough decision making to make game-play not feel random. X-Wing is a very good "boys' toys with rules" sort of game.  The enjoyment of this game is greatly heightened by being involved with the subject matter and writing a little story while playing. Keeps things fun. There are scenarios to help change things up beyond the normal dogfight if that begins to get stale.  The best thing about this game is that - unlike ANY miniature - you can have fun with 3 ships or 30 (if that's what you are in to).  But there is no requirement to spend hundreds of dollars on it to make a complete game.  The small skirmishes can be just as intense as an all out war. Kudos to Fantasy Flight for keeping things real.  Can't imagine ever wanting another miniatures game.

RATING: 10
This game hits the sweet spot for me, between the nerve-wrecking decision making of Miniature Wargames, and the easy accessibility of Boardgames.

If you are a fan of Star Wars you owe it to yourself to try this. It is amazing.

After MANY playthroughs, i'll drop the rating on this a little. It's good still, but what I have against it is a couple of things.

1.) Usually the first combat pass is often the game-deciding battle; few of my fights have twists with different players taking the leads at times.

2.) Some obvious Strategies are taking shape. Currently strength in numbers trumps Pilot skill; Quantity > Quality. I would hope to see that balanced out.

Here's to hoping for Wave 2.

RATING: 7
Part of me hates to give a game a 10 because I am a firm believer that nothing is perfect. But honestly, outside of the fact that there is no standard play mat and the starter box is ridiculously annoying with its cut out top, this game can do no wrong.

Such blind love for this game (its my #1) does deserve some explanation. So the reasons why the 10 is deserved:

1. Wife loves it and is always willing to play
2. Its just plain fun (rules are very well done and simple) and it gets "gotta get them all"   addicting. 
3. Its awesome trying to anticipate your opponent
4. The quality of the components are amazing!
5. My wife loves it!!!

Edit: after a couple of bad experiences that led to a game night flop, my love for this game deflated a bit. I actually went as far as to sell it off. I am still not sure whether I regret this or not and maybe that uncertainty means I did the right thing by deciding to stop adding ships to my collection and sell it instead.

RATING: 7
Pros:
- I am finding this core set slightly more balanced than the Force Awakens one, with Luke Skywalker nowhere near as powerful as Poe Dameron
- There are slightly more unique characters than in the Force Awakens one, especially on the Empire side.

Cons:
- It took us some time to realise that the X-Wings in both core sets had different command dials. So it is not possible to get Luke Swylwalker sitting in a more modern X-Wing for instance. Same on the Empire side.
- ships in the Force Awakens core set have more movement options.
- the value vs cost ratio for the old ships, especially the X-Wing, is very different to the new core set, meaning that for a game with a set amount of points, you wouldn't choose most of the ships and pilots of this core set vs the pilots and ships of the new core set. I think FFG could fix this easily, by reducing the cost of the ships and pilots in this core set by a couple of points.

RATING: 7.8
I have two copies of the base game.  This is enough for me to field about 65 points, though maybe 50 if I didn't use my other expansions.  I have barely enough space to fill the boxes while keeping the insert.  
  This game is a tactical dog fight simulation.  You command a squad of Star Wars themed fighters in a two dimensional shoot out, where out maneuvering your opponent is the difference between victory and defeat.  There is an element of luck to this game, but as quantity of shots matters most, luck is on the side of the aggressor. 
  The main problem with this game is it's price. Depending on how tricked out you want your fleet to be, you can easily drop hundreds of dollars on ships.

RATING: N/A
When X-Wing first was announced, I will admit I was a bit underwhelmed and, quite frankly, the game did not appeal to me at all.

However, as time passed and more expansion packs were released, X-Wing kept growing in popularity not only among the gaming community as a whole, but also for me personally.

Eventually, the game had become this "monstrosity" with a sea of expansions. X-Wing was featured on TableTop. My son kept carefully bringing up the question time and time again: "Are we going to get X-Wing?" A friend of mine kept asking the same thing. It was this odd paradox where it was becoming harder to resist buying into X-Wing, but also easier, since — knowing myself — I knew I would want to "have it all", were I to jump in, and that would get expensive fast.

In the end, I decided that I was not going to play X-Wing, that I was perfectly fine with "just" Imperial Assault, and that I had plenty of other games to enjoy.

And then — "stuff" happened ...

While I'm undecided as to whether I should thank you or curse you (whoever you are), my son thanks you. And, for that, I, too, thank you!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
One of the best games out there! If you're a Star Wars fan, it's a must!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Excellent lite miniatures skirmish wargame. Players secretly select how their ship (X-wing or Tie fighter) will move and then resolve shooting using a simple to-hit and save mechanic (using nice custom engraved dice) and applying several modifers that players must choose depending on their assesment of the tactical situation. Much of the game play is in out-guessing your opponent's movement choices to line up your ship for close range shots while avoiding them doing that to you.

Building and customizing your squadron for battle is a key component of the game (the meta-game).

Very good for multi-player per side battles.

Play is quick, the included pre-painted ships are excellent (although perhaps a bit expensive) as are all the chits and movement tokens. This is not a serious space combat simulation. Great fun!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The best competitive miniatures game at the moment. Short playtime makes it easy to fit in to your schedule and you only need a couple of ships at a time so carrying the squadron around is not a problem.

Mechanically, it is very solid. Using templates to move precisely keeps unnecessary arguments to a minimum. Rulebook (webpage version) and errata answer every question if the players just look them over.

FFG reacts to OP builds and tries actively to boost less flown ships with new upgrades. The game is very well balanced at the moment.

AUG 2017 EDIT: The design of the new ships is beginning to falter. The competitive side is more and more dependent on abusing the right card combos than careful flying. The game is still very good but high-level games are not as satisfying anymore to watch or play.

RATING: 7
UPDATE OCT 2, 2015:
I am back to enjoying this game, after a couple of recent sessions that really clicked. For one thing, the new Scum and Villainy faction acts as a counterbalance to the original teams: borrowing upgrade  cards between the three factions feels fun and thematic. I wouldn't want to juggle another system like this, but for now, I'm uping the grade, and working out ways to integrate it with my painted Imperial Assault set.

UPDATE OCT 14 2014: Features a problem inherent in many Fantasy Flight games. One player says Boom! Ha! Got you dead to rights! And another player says, "nope, because I have this teeny little card here that a person who dropped out of engineering school to play magic professionally before he went on to design games at Fantasy Flight says gives me a plus one defense that only triggers on the rare occasion when your plus one gives you a plus one on your plus one. So you missed." Thus, five minutes go by as you check the rules. I hear that people at Fantasy Flight aren't even compensated that well, they just like to plus one people to death.

--

Noooooooooo! This is money I don't have. And it's almost worth the money.

Then again, as someone with very little interest in Star Wars "deep cuts," I'm already looking at Wave Three ships and saying, "so, what's that, a bottle opener?" Wither the franchise?

RATING: 4

June 2015: I just don't like it enough to want to play it again. It's a lot of fiddle (set-up, storage, etc.) and far too long for what it is, despite the neat manoeuvring mechanic. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
It's a dogfight in a box.

This was my first foray into tabletop wargaming, and I could not be more pleased with the gameplay.

It combines the best elements of deckbuilding with a brilliant tactical maneuvering engine that is deceptively simple to pick up, yet takes time to master.

The theme is absolutely on point - the glorious space combat of the Star Wars original trilogy; with the odd detour into expanded universe territory.  The models are beautifully pre-painted, if a touch fragile at the "joints."

It's all about finding synergy between the various pilots, upgrades, and ships - and then being able to execute that gameplan in a dynamic environment.

I have to deduct a point from it for one simple reason:  The out-of-box experience is woefully insufficient.  You can't even run a proper 100pt squad game with the core set.  I automatically deduct a point from all my ratings if a game's core set comes with the recommendation to buy a second one to get started.  I'd rather pay more for a beefier core set with more options than that first taste to get you hooked and dropping cash on the expansions.

Marketing aside, this is a phenomenal title.  Every person I have introduced this to wants to play it again, and that's as strong a recommendation as I can think of.

RATING: 8
Matt, Nathan and I

Interesting movement with the templates. I've played some amount of miniature games in the past, but this one seems like more outright fun from a non-competitive standpoint than those have. As we're starting to get stronger lists going the game's depth has started to show more, loving the mechanics, can't find much of a flaw yet. As we're now approaching much stronger lists the games are still getting more interesting and tactical. 

I can get over dice in miniature games, but still get frustrated with them at times. While the movement is interesting the templates can be a bit finicky. We've had a few issues with the quality of the stands and having [-]3[/-] 4 of them snap on us. 

[-]Now that we're up to 100 point lists but still learning it's starting to be a bit slow, this feels like it'll be remedied with more practice.[/-] 
We have indeed gotten better at faster play, I feel like I need to set a tournament clock up though, just to make sure we keep improving our pace.

RATING: 10
Awesome miniatures; really the best I have seen for the price point.  IMHO, the cost, while not cheap, compares very favorably to other games with minis that are typically not painted, unassembled, and don't come with cards, counters, and stands.

Great theme; it simulates the fiction to a tee.

Easy play; after half a game you get the rules and are thinking about how to play well.

Fast play; reasonable size scenarios play out within 2 hours.

Decent depth; no, it isn't Whistling Death, but the combination of plotted moves, actions, special pilots, and buff cards keeps things interesting.  Missions, as opposed to straight-up duels, also add alot of depth.

Downsides:  I don't think the 100-pt 1:1 duel format is all that much fun, esp. the rebel vs. rebel and imperial vs. imperial battles.  The real fun is multiple players on each side in a big battle with some type of scenario to drive things, rather than just a cage-match.  If I rated the game based on the tournament scene, it would not be '10', it might be a '7' or lower.

RATING: 10
Edit: More games played and more factions coming out. From 9 to 10. This is how I wish Warhammer and Warhammer 40K was produced.

I love: The theme, the miniatures, the easy to use rules and template and the 1 model = many different pilots cards system of many different points value.

I don't mind: the dice randomness, the occasional Tie fighter blowing up very quickly and the small cards.
The price can seem to be a problem, until one realizes that it is cheaper than most other miniature games. 

The cons: X-wing suffers from a MTG effect, whereby some cards can only be found with some ships. Therefore, for total flexibility, you may want to buy all expansion ships at least once, even if you will not use them. Not a problem for casual play though, since you probably won't be making ultimate lists.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.4
The two paragraphs below are my original thoughts. After more plays somehow the game has just clicked. Randomness can be mitigated a great deal via movement and action allocation strategies. There are also some very nice synergies that can be utilized between various ship, pilot, and weapon combos. Now this may be my favorite 2 player game. We even played with 3 and it was great (2 guys played Imperial with 50 points each and the other guy got 100 as rebels). Setup is still a bear, so when we play it we usually plan to play 2 or 3 matches in a row only making minor adjustments in between. This gives me the "bang for my setup buck" that knocked the game for at first. 

This is not the worst game I have played, and I continue to get roped in to playing because my buddy has so much invested in the system. The game is just too clunky for what it is. 2 copies of the base game and numerous expansions equal loads of cards, tokens, etc to deal with. Setting up a basic 100 point game takes 15-30 minutes between unpacking, picking your pilots, secondary weapons, etc. Play can take anywhere from 30-60 minutes depending on strategy and dice. That is precisely the problem. I don't mind longer games where the dice can be mitigated (Stone Age, Yggdrasil, and Robinson Crusoe come to mind), but in this game they can't. So you spend all this time dragging hundreds of pieces out, crafting your ships, only to get 30 minutes in to the game and be blown away by incredibly bad or good die rolls. That is simply not fun.

The minis are well done and the rest of the components are nice quality, typical FF. Also, you can setup basic scenarios rather quickly that play in 15 minutes, so it is possible to have a 30 minute time from breaking it out to finishing a quick match, but these scenarios get old rather quickly. The escort the senator scenario, for example, basically consists of the rebel driving the senator straight across the table while the imperial side hopes to get lucky enough on die rolls to take him out. After many plays the die rolls do seem do even out some. Neither one of us win on a regular basis regardless of the strategy we use. I consider this to be a negative, however, as I would rather win based on strategical merit and good decision making than die rolls.

RATING: 7
Despite my general dislike of the Wings of War series (and games with measuring in general), the theme intrigued me enough to give this one a shot. In general, I was pleasantly surprised. 

Each player receives a fleet of various ships and cards to go with them. Giving each ship a special ability provides excellent flavor and army-building potential, even before adding in the upgrade cards. Players will then plan their movement, with more difficult maneuvers putting strain on the ship such that it must make an easy maneuver before attempting another difficult one. Players must also decide whether to have their ships get defensive bonuses, dice bonuses, extra maneuvers, etc. All these choices do a good job of creating depth without feeling overwhelming. 

What really sets this apart from Wings of War (and makes it better) is the vast amount of units involved. A failed bluff or missed read in a game involving one-on-one combat can be absolutely disastrous. Spreading these bluffs over a whole fleet though creates an experience much more towards the middle of the bell curve. It seems to better reward bluffing in balance with tactical movement. That said, the endgame is weak because of this. Once players are down to only a ship or two each, the decisions are much less interesting. It's an oddly anti-climactic game. Another minor drawback, but easily houseruled, is the prohibition on pre-measuring before moving. Rewarding spatial and estimating skills seems very out of place in a game of tactical movement and dice rolling. 

Despite the comparatively boring late game, the frantic early action is very exciting. The pilots for each ship make it easy to personify the action, which is very fun. This is a game that seems to really require customization to be at its best and should lend itself well to tournament play. But for the kitchen table, someone with an interest in constructing these fleets will be a virtual necessity.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
“You’re all clear kid. Now lets blow this thing and go home!” - Han Solo

GAMEPLAY
The X-Wing Miniatures Game brings the dog fighting action of the Star Wars Universe to the tabletop, Specifically the Episodes 4, 5, and 6 timeframe. The game flows well from turn to turn as the game turn has four phases. One, Planning phase, secretly choose your ships’ movement. Two, Activation phase, move your ships and perform an action to help your ship survive and improve your chances to hit. Three, Combat phase, resolve you shooting for the turn. Four, End phase, clean up the game space. The planning phase offers a fun battle of wits with your opponent as your try to predict their moves and line up you shots. Each class of ship is restricted in their choices of manuevers. The Tie Fighters are fast but have restrictions on short turns with no shields. The X-Wings are generally mobile and have some shields. The Y-Wings are slow very durable and have lots of shield. Most of the turn is spent during the combat phase to resolve shooting. Ships have attack and defense dice. The die rolls can be modified by actions and pilots special abilities. Damage points are scored on each ship and critical hits will cause disruptions to the ship and the pilot.

X-Wing immerses you in the Star Wars setting and gives a fun fast gameplay experience. Having the game in two dimensions was clearly in the interest of keeping the game moving. A more hardcore dogfighting simulation can be found in Wings of Glory a WWII miniature game (Which I also recommend).

COMPONENTS
The models are well detailed, simply painted models. If you are a model painter the painting can easily be improved on, but the out of the box quality will have most fans smiling. The expected high quality Fantasy flight production is in evidence here, thick cardboard for the movement rulers, everything is easy to read, and the art is top notch. All of the stats and abilities are clear and easy to distinguish on the pilot cards.

THEME
Full of star wars. Get to fly as your favorite character from the movie when you are the good guys, Luke and Biggs. While playing the imperials the pilots get sufficiently generic evil names such as Mauler Mithel and Night Beast. The first wave of expansions add Characters with each ship including Wedge and Darth Vader. The Second coming early 2013 will add the Millennium Falcon and Slave one.

WHO IS IT FOR?
Anyone who loves Star Wars will enjoy this game. Players 10 and up can enjoy the game. The quick turns will keep younger players engaged.

The game out of the box will let players experience three basic scenarios which are all fun and different to play. Be for-warned though. As with most miniatures games, to play larger more spectacular battles, multiple expansions are necessary. The game recommends battle of 100 points. Each pilot card has a point value with weapon and droid upgrades available. 100 points battle require between four and six ships per side. The base set comes with 1 X-Wing and 2 Tie Fighters.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
(12/19/2015) Comment based on one play.

This is a great miniatures game that conveys the feel of a dogfight in the Star Wars universe. The designer has managed to take the basic mechanisms from Wings of War and improve upon them, to make a fast-playing, intense, and completely customizable game.

I played Wings of War nearly eight years ago, and was annoyed at the lack of consistency of the maneuvering through the use of cards. The play seemed forced and artificial, with a rather sloppy tolerance. In X-Wing, there are sets of maneuvering gauges that help with the movement of the models. Movement usually follows a 0 deg, 45 deg, or 90 deg turn, along with a movement "speed" ranging from 1 to 5 units. The desired maneuver gauge is placed in front of the base of the model. The model is then moved to the other end of the gauge, such that the aft of the base of the model touches the end.

What is a stroke of genius is the inclusion of "maneuver dials", similar to the sailing dials in Pirate's Cove, where each player secretly and simultaneously selects one of a handful of maneuvers. Every fighter in the game has a unique dial, each with a limited menu of basic and advanced maneuvers. The players, in initiative order reveal and execute their maneuver, along with selecting an action, such as focusing, target lock, evasion, or barrel rolling. If an enemy fighter is within their field of vision, they roll a number of attack dice depending on their fighter. The target also rolls a number of defense dice depending on their fighter as well. Hits are negated with evasion. Resulting hits are applied against shields and structure ratings of the target fighter.

With only two or three "hit points" per fighter, an introductory 2 vs 1 dogfight can be concluded in 30 minutes or less. The play is quick, but the spatial and vector decisions involved can be challenging--one really feels like they are flying an X-Wing or a TIE fighter! There is an element of luck with the dice throws, but thematically makes sense. Rules are short and easy to explain, and the game concepts are not that complicated. This is a good introduction to the world of miniatures gaming, due to the clean, simple rules, along with tools that allow for precise plotting. Initial rating is "8". I think this system has great promise, but realize it is a collectible. If a friend has it, I'll gladly play it, but will not spend a cent to get addicted to this gamer crack.

RATING: 8
[floatleft][size=18][b]AWWWW[/b][/size]

[imageid=266785]
[size=18][b]YEEEEAH[/b][/size][/floatleft]
I'm not really a [i]Star Wars[/i] fan—it's just that 89% of my childhood consisted of nothing but [i]Star Wars[/i], [i]The Empire Strikes Back[/i] and [i]Return of the Jedi[/i].  I was 10 when my Mom took me and a friend to see some weird space movie on opening day...  If you were near that age and walked into it blind—[i]with a completely naked psyche[/i]—you get it.  It was like being pulled hot off the anvil and thrust into a screaming slave's belly...  Tempered in death and rebirth; shocking and permanently formative.  A fulcrum point for generational shift.

As a kid I built X-wing and TIE fighter model kits until my fingers bled and I hallucinated glue-fume Jawas; I would have strangled the children & little people inside the rough brown cloaks with my inflatable lightsaber for a game like this.  (Still would.)  So to say that the perfectly detailed, tiny model ships resonate would be a massive understatement.

Again, I am not a fan; I find anything other than the original three movies—the "Expanded Universe", crappy novelizations, comics, Prequels, video games, etc., etc., ad nauseam—to be baby laxative.

But [i]X-Wing[/i] is the pure, uncut stuff, a high as dangerous as time travel and I'm 10 again.

RATING: 7
The same concept as Wings of War, but much better designed and with a much cooler theme.

X-Wing offers a DECENT damage probability distribution. As dice results are compared, the distribution is closer to gaussian, whereas in Wings of War there are too many zeroes and too many nasty cards (the auto-kill, fives, etc...) that bring high-variance nasty randomness.

X-Wing offers a lot more control, as you plan every move after your last move. In WoW, you plan three moves after your last three moves: no one can predict the opponent's third movement, and planes usually do weird things and engaging an enemy is very difficult, wasting your time flying in circles.

X-Wing offers a lot of mechanical variety, reusing the same miniature with different stats thanks to the Pilot cards. Wings of War does the exact opposite, having lots of redundant miniatures with the bloody same stats. No Pilot distinction in a game called "Famous Aces"? How is that?

X-Wing gets rid of the inconvenience of using cards to plan your maneuvers. The slider disks are perfect to plan your movement. 

X-Wing is the game that Wings of War should had been. 

I have:

2 X-Wings
2 Y-Wings
2 A-Wings
2 B-Wings

4 TIE
2 TIE-Advanced
2 TIE-Interceptor
1 TIE-Bomber

1 Millenium Falcon
1 Slave-0
1 Lambda Shuttle

RATING: 5.5
I'm not really a miniatures fan but I'll admit that the pre-painted ships are nice (presuming you're willing to re-mortgage your house in order to buy them all) and the movement mechanism is as smooth and clever as it is unoriginal.

My only real problem with the game is that I think that the multitude of card options gets in the way more than it contributes to what's otherwise quite a decent, light wargame. Obviously the cards lend a great deal of variety and I'm sure they're great if you want that collectible deck building feel but that's just not an element I'm very interested in seeing in a tactical miniatures game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This was such a fun game to learn. It comes with two rule books; condensed and elaborate. The game is beautifully designed so that you can start playing immediately. And that is very appealing because the miniatures in this game are phenomenal. I can't praise this game enough for its high quality components. And since everyone knows at least something of the Star Wars universe, it's easy for new players to jump right in.

One side plays the Empire, the other plays the Rebels. This is a tactical miniatures game where movement is key. Like most miniatures games, both sides agree to an allotted set amount of points. You then spend these points building up a squadron of different ships, pilots, and upgrades. The more skilled the pilot...the more points you'll have to spend. But you just might want to because the person with the highest pilot skill gets to move last, and shoot first. Whereas taking a lot of lower skilled pilots lets you have that many more opportunities to fire each turn.

The customizable nature of this game gives it great replayability. You'll never play the same game twice.
