=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The design and execution just makes me straight-up smile. Full disclosure that I am one of the biggest Star Wars fans anywhere, but I don't think that matters if you want a great game.

The miniatures look great, especially for the cost, and this is maybe the most rewarding AND accessible miniatures game I know of for someone just getting into the genre. Admittedly, it is not an all-in-one box miniatures game, but the depth you get is superb with the different units.

Combat and play dynamics are very fun, with enough luck present, but still skills backing it up. I love the different cards for pilots and upgrades and the dynamics of rolls for hits, evasion and other tactics.

It is also quite fun to put together a storage kit for the game and even your own regulation 3'x3' board. I painted and laminated my own with a black background and space illustrations.

This game is perfect and wears well. PS - be prepared to spend at least $150, in my opinion, to eventually get enough components for long-term lasting interest, although the starter will definitely let you determine if you will like it or not.

RATING: 8
Such a fun game! The mechanics are simple, the miniatures are amazing, and the gameplay is quick and fierce. These only slightly detract from the game, though, and I would highly recommend it to any fan of Star Wars, mini gaming, or casual fan.

RATING: 9
OWNED SINCE 2013
A really exciting game. Even my daughter, who usually does not play board games, likes this one. It is easy to learn and fast to set up. My first couple of games were fun, but they could feel too long towards the end. But, this was because I was playing with my small kids who, at age 7 and below, do not understand the game tactics too well. This made the games very one-sided. Now, after having played this game with another adult, this game is very good. Decisions feel meaningful and games can be very, very close. Also, I now have more ships. I think you need at least 100 pts. worth of ships, for each side, to really have the full experience. I can't wait to get more ships.
     EDIT: I have many of the ships now, and must say they all seem balanced in there own way and none of them have lost their importance because of new expansions- an amazing compliment for any game that there is no power creep, I hope FFG can keep it like this longer. Regardless of what people say and rate each ship I recommend you get what you want because I have found peoples opinions to be very wrong at times. I have enjoyed many ships that others hate. I really look forward to scenarios, and am interested in the big ships if it can make great scenarios. I plan to continue to buy more ships, not that I need them, but I want them and they add a lot to the game's variety. Playing with different builds gives the game new flavors I enjoy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
2-players game (yes, 2 players, if you are 3 and desperate to play, ok, do it, but remember that I told you) in which every player controls a bunch of SW ships and engage in a close space combat. The game is fun, I enjoy it, the ships are very nice, the idea of the game, even if not original, it is excellent: to plan in advance the movements and actions and then resolve and check if there are any interactions between ships, between a ship and an asteroid or whatever. That is very fun. But, and it is a huge "but", the issue is that, once you start buying more ships, and trust me, you will, it becomes more and more complex to prepare a game and the set up is a bit of a nightmare. You do not only have to choose which ships will be part of your fleet, you need to decide how many abilities, characters and weapons are going to carry every one of those ships and, every time you buy an extra ship, it comes with a lot of cards that have to be added to the collection.
The real approach of this game, is to think as if you were going to play warhammer 40k (or that type of game, Flames of War, Bolt Action... you understand), I mean, part of the experience is to plan the fleet in advance. Maybe decide with your friend: "400 points", and each one of you get to the table with your army ready, if not, get ready for more than an hour of preparation. Aside from that, the game is very good
Positive:
1. The minis
2. The mechanics
3. Very fun
Negative:
1. The set up is very tedious if the fleets are not prepared in advance

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
The core game is the same as Wings of War so a fun game, however in true FFG fashion they added all kinds of little nifty things here and there and it comes out quite well I think, you do have more choices to make here but of course its still mostly a tactical affair with a LARGE luck factor. 

So the SW license got a good treatment IMO and the theme does stand out, you do have to hand it to FF as much as they are milking it. (REALLY think 3 ships in the base game is criminal, and then who wants to buy 2 core sets to get more dice, movement markers etc and you end up with duplicate ships? Yuck) 

So a nice thematic game of bluff and second-guessing what your opponent will do (where he will fly). It uses simultaneous programmed actions like Roborally, and everyone playing has mostly all the same move possibilities. You reveal your moves and then move your ship accordingly, do an action if you want to and can, and then if planes are within range firing occurs. You feel the theme at work when you just pass by an opponent and must circle back to try and get him in your sights, only your not sure which way to circle, and things like droids helping you to heal, barrel roll evasions, and more. 

The one thing that seemed a little weird was the strong Pilots with high numbers fighting weak pilots didn’t really have any advantage except attacking first, which is important of course but I would have thought something like a Pilot who attacks a weaker Pilot gets to re-roll one miss each attack (easy houserule if wanted anyway).  Other than that lots of nifty add-ons here to WoW like targeting, shields, stress, etc good stuff. 

Only played with 2 and thought it was quite good that way (where as the core WoW game needs more), playing in teams should also be a fun option I would think too.

RATING: 10
I love this game. Full disclosure, I'm a huge Star Wars OT fan. Then again, fuller disclosure, I'm also a very image-conscious 25-year-old.

That being said, I still somehow am propelled time and again to walk into Barnes & Noble and purchase ship expansions ... usually being rung up by the same guy who judges me every single time. BUT IT'S TOTALLY WORTH IT.

I had never played any other miniature/wargame type game before X-Wing and, at first, I tried to resist the temptation to obsess about my miniatures ... my play area ... my pilot cards ... etc. Then I gave in and I haven't looked back.

This game not only is VERY fun to play (feels well thought out and balanced), but is SOOOO beautiful. I know various people who only collect the miniatures just because they are so well-made. Not only that, but everything is to scale ... which is just awesome. And we're talking about not only ships from the films, but also expanded universe ships. Ever wondered what the Outrider looks like next to the Moldy Crow? Me too. It's stupid cool.

This was also the game that introduced me to FFG who are, by the way, an amazing company. Aside from their quality of product being phenomenal (the widely accepted opinion), they really do care about their customers. I recently misplaced my Tie Interceptor expansion dial and they sent me a replacement free of charge. It's stuff like that that keeps me spending all of my disposable income on their products. 

TLDR: Great game with beautiful components from an awesome company. Fans of Star Wars, it's a no-brainer. Everyone else, worth at least the core set.

RATING: 5
2012-10-23

Initial rating: 5.0 (October 2012)

In theory, X-wing miniatures would be a great game for me. It has all the ships I always wanted to flight in the Star Wars Universe. In practice the gameplay is awkward and it doesn’t fulfill me. I’m a huge Star Wars fan, but that’s not enough to enjoy X-Wing Miniatures. I also don’t like Wings of War, so this kind of game is not for me. But I DO like this a bit more than Wings of War.

The miniatures are gorgeous (as expected from FFG) and they will be a money pit for the players who buy this game. :devil: Fortunately I’m not in that camp. 

I like that you only plan 1 maneuver and execute, for me, this adds another layer of tactical thinking and IMO reduces the luck I found in WoW. In Wings of War you have to play 3 maneuvers which I always disliked, but this come with a cost, the game is paced more slowly that Wings of War so it can take a longer game to finish. Also it has a lot of luck via the dice rolls. In our game the dice rolls were the determining factor in who won and who lost and if that holds true for all the games the rating will go even down. 

The game can be explained very quickly and plays under 1 hour.

The X-wing miniatures seem a lot smaller then the Tie Fighter ones. I wonder if they are not done at the same scale?

Bottom line if I’m going to play dogfighting, I prefer to play it in a videogame format. X-Wing miniature has great chrome but have little of interest under the hood. I won’t buy it and I don’t plan to play this often if ever.

Current Rating: 5.0

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The title hits it spot on. X-Wing, the miniatures games is an action packed recreation of the starfighter battles we came to love as kids. 

The miniatures are reasonably cheap and surprisingly well prepainted for their price. The core rules are easy and fast to comprehend, the execution swift and uncomplicated. The cinematic flair palpable due to the simultanuous planning, movement and the shooting sequences. 

It's the special rules that add (or convolute, depending on your point of view and the amount you like to introduce into your matches) even more spice into it. 

Due to the continued support of FFG there is also an abundance of ships and fighters and even small capital ships (like the Blockade Runner or Rebel transport) available for purchase, with the majority of them centered mostly around the Galactic Civil War.

It provides 3 game modes:
 
1. Dogfight: Where you have squadrons of up to 8 ships for each side battling it out against the other (Which is the default tournament system, btw.)
2. Cinematic: Where you play missions with sometimes unbalanced squadron sizes, but lots of neat mission objectives to fulfill (escort, sabotage, scout, capture the flag)
3. Epic: Where you have tripple or more the standard amount of ships on each side, including the capital ships 
 
Also, there is a very active FFG-supported League and Tournament Scene worldwide operating, so that there is almost always a chance to get into the competetive side of the game. 

I myself have come to see the game to better be played on a casual approach with missions, as a self created campaign or in its Epic incarnation, as the (dogfight) tournament system has become a rather fast paced race between armour and weapons and hence primary the participating player in it just the cashcow for the franchise. 

(This is due to the equipment cards system that provide the games special rules: Some fighters need special equipment cards that aren't included in their own expansion but in another fighter pack [and often in one of the opposing factions} thus forcing the player to buy into the other faction as well if he wants to be able to compete.) 

Once you cut yourself off from the "need to compete", and open yourself up to a more mission centric play, by reenacting duels with your favourite heroes or daring objective themed battles (more or less house ruling the game), it's there where X-Wing really shines. Of course, a quickly thrown down dogfight on the kitchen table doesn't hurt either.

Bonus feels, if you play the Star Wars soundtrack in the background and add a sound-app to the game. 

X-Wing TMG is in fact a Star Wars fans wet dream come true. Though it has to be approached with love and care to really enjoy it to its fullest.

RATING: 7
Elegantly designed, high quality components, and most importantly great fun!

All of the various expansions are dizzying though. And even if you limit yourself to the very basic types of ships, the various different pilots and ship modification cards can get rather bothersome and too fiddly.

Thankfully though, you can ignore all of that and just use the basic ship stats and abilities! I think those upgrade cards and such are mostly there to prevent the game from getting stale for those who play the same ships repeatedly and don't continuously get more and more expansions.

Edit: Sold off my whole collection. Unfortunately this game has rapidly suffered from "Magic syndrome", where it's become impossible to find anyone willing to play casually. It seems you either need to buy all the latest stuff constantly and play competitively, or not at all...

A big shame, as this was a nice game. But like hell I'm going to put up with this foolishness. I suppose FFG makes big bucks with constant expansions and promotional events, but it really sours me as a player who doesn't want to turn a single game into a life-encompassing obsession.

RATING: 6
My plays of Wings of War were enjoyable, I rate it a '7'. Did my memory betray me and Wings of War isn't as fun as I remembered it? My three plays of Star Wars: X-Wing were ok but nothing to write home about. Only after reading [thread=865799]this review[/thread] I understood what happened.

The thing I enjoy in Wings of War most is the programmed movement part. I enjoy the tactical challenge of outmanoeuvering the other guy. X-Wing replaced the programming part with a single simultaneous selection of movement. Single movements will differ much more than in WoW raising the chaos/surprise factor noticeably.
 
The main improvement of X-Wing is the strategic customization of your fleet. Ships are very different, they can be customized with weapons, pilot skills can be improved etc. In WoW, the different planes are more a different flavour than a different meal, battles are smaller. To be honest, this customization is rather discouraging for me. I don't like to enter the game and already having lost because of a weak setup.

To be fair, I rate it a '6' as I like the basic principle.

RATING: 8
[Wings of War]
Here was my problem with Wings of War. You could have games which lasted forever, because players made 3 moves in advance and you couldn't react to each other's moves. So both planes could drift really far apart, and it would take a long time to circle round.

[X-Wing]
X-Wing plays very similarly to Wings of War. Fortunately, the long templates and the ability to make one move at a time (reacting to other players) makes this game fast and brutal. The game is easy-to-learn, easy-to-reset and a lot of fun to play.

RATING: 10
Played this game with my brother this past weekend and both of us had a blast, even just using the basic ships that come in the core set. It's easy to make this 2-player game a game for even more players by teaming up and assigning individual ships to each player. And once you start adding on the ships from the expansions, your options for play are limitless. By our second game, my brother and I were already dreaming up custom rules scenarios with moving asteroids, etc. Your imagination is the limit in this super easy to learn strategy game, with super fun mechanics which perfectly capture the thematic elements. For added fun, download a Star Wars sound effect app and go crazy with laser blasts and engine howls to make you and your friends feel like you're flying around the depths of space. The Core Set has everything you need to play, but I would recommend picking up two sets, or a copy of the new Force Awakens Core Set, to immediately increase the size of your squads and give each player a set of dice and maneuver templates.

RATING: 6
[size=12][b]Top 200 board games list[/b][/size]

[size=12][b]Why I like Star Wars: X-Wing Miniatures Game[/b][/size]
+ The game is easy to teach
+ The mechanics work alright. 
+ There is high player involvement
+ There is decent replayability
= The game requires meaningful decisions to win the game in terms of how you move the ship and use your special abilities to mitigate bad dice rolls. 
+ The Star Wars theme works well. 
+ The game is short enough.

[size=12][b]Fixable dislikes in regards to Star Wars: X-Wing Miniatures Game[/b][/size] 
/ I wish the map was more threatening with say moving asteroids. there seem to be variants in the forums that address this problem.
/ The game seems to lack a cooperative 2 v 2 or 3 v 3 mode. I did some research and there seem to be variants that address this complaint. If there are not then you could probably just divide the ships among the players. 

[size=12][b]Why I dislike Star Wars: X-Wing Miniatures Game[/b][/size]
- I was not a fan of some of the ships. I think that the designer could have halved the number of ships and improved the viability of the ships. 

[size=12][b]VERDICT:[/b] Sometimes willing to play this game[/size]

RATING: 5
This game is not necessarily bad if you like analog miniatures games. Unfortunately, I prefer playing with miniatures in a digital space. Besides being very unlucky in the game I played I don't thinks at first glance that the game is broken or unbalanced.

I was a great fan of the "tie fighter" video game and I know a lot about star wars dog fighting. It reproduced slightly the same feeling because you have to judge the amount of movement you need to catch your opponent. So you are never sure how you are going to end up after movement.

The first problem I have with this game is that it is a star fighter only game. And if you do that, then you have failed to learn the whole strategy behind star wars navy. Capital ships are essential, and just having star fighters is plain boring.

The second problem is that it's an EXTREMELY EXPENSIVE game. You pay almost 15$ for 1 miniature. Come on, even in hero scape, you ended-up with 2 squads of 3 units for that price. So if you want to seriously play this game, you need to be a rich guy that does not know what to do with his money since you are going to spend many hundreds of dollars.

So I don't think it's a bad game, if you actually like analog miniature games.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Uh oh, another money-pit coming from Fantasy Flight.  The miniatures are nicely painted and the game is pretty tight.  Each side gets the same amount of points to spend for ships/pilots/mods.  Wings of War style of fighting to some degree in that each person selects a maneuver at the same time but only one move in advance.  Lowest ranked pilot flies first while the highest ranked pilot fires first - very important to keep those factors in mind as you maneuver.

RATING: 9
This is hands down my favourite game. No doubt about it. I like Star Wars and some of the more iconic characters, but I'm not a fanatic. The gameplay itself is what keeps me engaged.

PROS:
-Easy to learn, hard to master.
-Simultaneous planning of maneuvers in activation phase.
-Maneuver templates for movement instead of hexes or squares. Love this!
-Very balanced considering all that's out for the game. And the designers are always working to keep every ship relevant.
-It's a dice game, but skill will win over luck.
-Production value. The miniatures are amazing.
-Replayability beyond dogfighting (which I'm still not tired of) with many official missions and not to mention fan-made ones like The Heroes of Aturi Cluster (http://dockingbay416.com/campaign/)

CONS:
-Pricey if you are a completionist.
-If you're getting into the game now, all the upgrades and pilots might be overwhelming.
-It IS a dice game and sometimes you set up that perfect shot and... roll all blanks!

Re-rated from a 9.75 to 9. The bloat due to the business model is ruining the game and power creep is real.

RATING: 8

And if you really want the full experience, make sure you play the Star Wars film score in the background.  My only complaint is that the smaller miniatures, especially the tie fighters and x-wings, are fragile.  Regardless, this game is worth every penny and then some.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
On paper, I should like this game a lot more than I actually do.  It's good great looking miniatures, and it captures very well the experience of a dogfight, especially videogame dogfights like the ones in Red Baron, Freespace, or X-Wing.  Instead, there are four things that detract from my enjoyment:  1) I have played dogfight videogames before, I have already mined this vein and I no longer enjoy as much circling around each other waiting to get the broadshot, or the opportunity to tail the enemy, or whatever slight advantage one needs to win the dogfight.  2)  Without a grid on the plying surface, I have a hard time visualizing where my fighter and the opponent's fighter will next be.  I understand that this probably gets better with knowledge and practice, but it's like playing blind. 3) I usually dislike resolving combat though dice rolling.  I disliked it in Risk, and I dislike it in the Battle Cry type games, and this is no exception.  There is something unsatisfying and grating about tactics being irrelevant due to a bad roll of dice.  4)  Time investment.  Clearly this is a game that would require significant time investment and repeated plays to become reasonably good at it (for example to learn to better visualize movement).  5)  Cost -- exorbitant.  This last factor plays a stronger role because I usually am reluctant to like games that I cannot afford, probably a mixture of jealousy and self preservation.  So in spite of the excellent components, the good theme integration, the good mechanics, the bluffing and deduction element, the spatial element, the skill component, the customizability -- all elements that I usually like very much in a game -- I would only play this occasionally as a short dogfight, and will not ask for it unless I am in the mood for this type of experience and ready to win or lose playing blind and with my fate in a roll of dice. This last

RATING: 10
Wing of Star Wars is as good as the parent games in every way and has the added coolness of old school Star Wars. 

I like the pilot Actions better, and the templates/dial are way easier than the card decks from WoW.

It is pricey, but so are all mini's based games. 

Really best as a 2 player, but larger numbers work ok. 

If I had to sum it up I think x-wing takes a great flight sim engine from wing of war and adds a game on top of that.  Streamlining the movement to be perhaps less realistic (these are space ships) but simpler, and adding in the decisions of the pilot actions to add a lot of fun to the game. 

The deck building aspect of this also adds to the game.

Love it.

RATING: 9.3
Star Wars.  

Amazing mini sculpts.

Agonizing tactical decisions.

Oh man!

This is so different than any other game I own or have played.  It's refreshing to have it fill a niche that no other game does!  The high quality components and elegant rules are outstanding, and the Star Wars theme seals the deal!

Occasionally measuring movements gets annoying...and sometimes we accidentally knock the ships a bit out of position, which is no good!  Still, the movement mechanic is like no other game I have, so overall I'm still a fan.

RATING: 7
Initially sceptical of this being a straight 'Wings of War' clone, but it improves on that basic template to create a fast, tactical game of reading your enemy, positioning and good old luck. Fleet building is simple and the game can be easily scaled for new players.

(Edit) I'm actually starting to miss Wings of War's focus on manoeuvring and semi-deterministic damage, as it can be very frustrating and anti-climactic to out-fly someone in X-Wing, only to roll crap dice. Also too many turrets these days. Not sure how I feel about this one at present.

(Further Edit) I sold up. Couldn't justify so much money tied up in ships for a 2-player game I was falling out of love with. Had a fun few years, won some local tourneys, so no hard feelings. Bought SO MUCH STUFF from the proceeds of sale!

RATING: 8
This game really is fantastic.  The theme is clearly awesome if one loves Star Wars, the gameplay is supurb, and the components are an incredible value for their detail and quality.
The reason I don't give it a 10 is because setup, if you don't already know what you want to field (and even then),can be and often is very long.  Cleanup is a chore as well.  Storage solution is a must for this game, if you go beyond a core set or two.
Gameplay is brisk, exciting, and is fun for people to simply watch.  This to me really helps, as those not in the game can spectate, yet not get bored as in standard board games.

RATING: 2
streamlined version of Wings of War. Buying it because the theme will attract more players than WOW.

Update- as a long time fan of both Star Wars and wings of war this seemed perfect. I've introduced the game to many gaming groups and the result is never encouraging. The game just doesn't end dramatically! 

I was very excited about the changes to the core system but after replaying wings of we I prefer it's I less system. I don't know what to do with this game now, thematically this game is more appealing then wings of war but WOW seems to be more satisfying!

Maybe the new ships will come with new scenarios that will spice up the game...

Update: I've bought all the ships and still haven't been impressed by the scenarios or how the actions work. This game will end up on ebay or donated to my office soon.

Update: this game has been completely replaced by GF9:s Tanks game. Real tabletop gaming (with terrain), no hard to understand actions, terminology, or custom dice... Just fast and fun epic battles.

RATING: 9
Wings of War is a great system, we loved it, but got phased out eventually, as it way too often came down to circling around each other endlessly. With getting rid of the limitations of historical and physical accuracy, the game became more intense and dynamic, while remained realistic in its own universe. 

I don't care much for SW, but loved to play SW: Tie Fighter back in the days, and the fighters have kept their distinguished characteristics amazingly well. The customizable fighters and pilots, paired with the easy and intuitive control adds a lot to the WoW system, and the result is a fantastic tactical game, which easily can handle ten or so fighters simultaneously. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
As a Star Wars fanatic, and a lover of games where you pilot an air/space craft, I LOVE X-Wing! Over the past 4-5 years, this game has received a TON of expansions featuring ships and characters from the Star Wars universe, and some that are really obscure knowledge from Legends. The only thing I don't like about this game (which says a lot, actually) is that the competitive scene is too meta-driven, and sometimes you just want to play for fun instead. Aside from that, X-Wing has everything you're looking for in a great Star-Wars themed game!

RATING: N/A
This game is a tough one for me.

I *love* Star Wars, and the notion of this tactical dogfighting game with the famous ships I loved and more coming out every few months was FAR too tempting to pass up.  My friend Brian got me into this, and he had most of the Rebel AND Imperial ships.  Not wanting to copy what he already had available for play, I ended up buying all of the newly available Scum & Villainy ships in one fell swoop, before we played the game maybe 3 times.  It then sat for over a year, for lack of people to play with, and also due to not having time.  Brian is imminently going to move to Utah for at least 8 months of each year, and he actually sold his holdings of this game in favor of Star Wars Armada.

It is also worth mentioning I didn't really enjoy the dogfighting as it actually played out, as many times this just led to a handful of ships juking successfully turn after turn.  Exciting to start, boring as hell to finish any given playthrough.

Shucks.

I ended up deciding to sell my holdings in this game to my friend Jason who is getting into it, and we have actually settled into playing through the player-made coop campaign every few weeks, and I love that.  MUCH More fun that the interminable dogfighting to me; and I don't own it any more so there is no more temptation to dump money into it.

(Written 4/25/16)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.8
I have only played a couple of games of this so far and as I have a large-ish and growing collection Wings of Glory: WW1 Airplane Packs, Wings of Glory: WW2 Airplane Pack and aircraft for Axis & Allies Air Force Miniatures: Angels 20 the last thing I need is another aerial combat game. This is that game!

This game has a great theme, I was a little kid when the Star Wars movies came out and have always been fond of the Star Wars universe. This game offers the chance to play out space battle in that universe with wonderful miniature X-wings, Y-wings as well as a variety of TIE fighters and suchlike.

The game itself is pretty easy to learn. Anyone who has played Wings of Glory: WW1 Duel Pack would find a lot of the concepts to be pretty familiar. Each vessel is assigned an action (the breadth of actions available is determined by the capabilities of each ship) in secret each turn and in reverse pilot skill order executes that action and then may take another action depending on ship capabilities and/or pilot attributes. Once all actions have been executed those ships able to shoot then shoot at any eligible targets through rolling the specialist dice. These shots may be avoided again by rolling specialist dice dependent on the manoeuvrability of each vessel and pilot abilities.

The game itself plays well and is fast and fun. The individual pilot skills and ship upgrades can be altered each game (there is a points system to construct your forces) which gives a fair bit of variety and replayability to this game. Note that there is no consideration given to altitude so it is very much a two dimensional battle but that’s okay as it makes it much simpler without detracting very much at all from the experience. The miniatures themselves are superb and really look the part. They are comparatively fragile so be careful around small children but, gee, as I say, they look great.

This game looks to be well supported and has a pretty big following as far as I can gather. I can see myself getting into this one, no doubt to the annoyance of Mrs Fish. Still, when the Little Fish are a bit older I am sure they’ll love playing this with their old man. So, it’s an investment in a happy family future, isn’t it?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Star Wars: X-Wing ist zwar ein Miniaturen Spiel, jedoch mit relativ bersichtlichen Regeln und einem leichten Einstieg. Mit dem Basis-Set kann man sich einen guten Überblick, über das Spiel und seine Mechaniken schaffen. Im Grunde geht es um Weltraumschlachten im Star Wars Universum, jedoch von der Größe eher an kleinere "Dog Fights" erinnernd. Mit einem Papp-Rad stellt man zu Beginn eines Zuges die Flugroute seiner Schiffe ein, dadurch entsteht ein Überraschungsmoment und es gilt, vorauszuplanen und den Gegner zu durchschauen. Ausrüstungsgegenstände, Piloten und Bewaffnung sorgen für unglaublich viel Abwechslung. Die Miniaturen sind vorbemalt und machen einen sehr hochwertigen Eindruck, wie auch der Rest des Spielmaterials. Aber X-Wing ist mit seinen unzähligen Erweiterungen auch ein Geld- und Ressourcenfresser (Platz!), auf den man sich einlassen muss.

RATING: 6
[i]X-Wing[/i] is a very good Ariel space battle miniatures game! The overall game play is tight and simple to learn, the movement system is near perfect (pending those all too convenient 'whoops! knocked it, now I'm in range' moments..), the combat is random and often dynamic and it just looks incredible!

Unfortunately the more time that goes by the more fed up I get of it!

The Star Wars theme just doesn't excite me that much despite the amazing looking minis! This has been offset somewhat by the release of the Scum faction which has brought several interesting looking expanded universe ships into play, but there's several themes that are similar I would have rather played.

I've also always felt that X-Wing is very prone to 'gaming'. If you are just playing casually- throwing together something random and having fun with it, its a real blast, but try to play against someone competitively and the horrible meta-game comes into play, looking for every loop hole, strength and rule that can be exploited to the fullest. The internet is awash with people ranting about the current meta and its most recent game breaking builds and strategies. Its exhausting, and it saps the fun for people like me who just want to have fun with it.

The worst turn off though is the never ending expansions. [i]This game is never going to stop.[/i] Fantasy Flight Games will keep putting out wave after wave of new ships for all eternity, and I don't want to go any further with it. Owning just one ship from each wave must have reached £1000 at retail now, or damn near close. I've played the game 30 odd times, nowhere near enough to justify that kind of money. 'Just don't buy the new stuff then', I hear you say. Well that brings me back to complaint number 2- the meta-game demands I do, otherwise I will not be able to keep up with the newest combos, upgrades and fixes to my older ships that's making everyone else stronger. I feel I have two choices left- either abandon the game and only play it with casual gamers or stop buying stuff and play with just what I already have- leading to me losing every game I play against the still active users who are forever gaining newer and stronger stuff.

This has understandably soured my attitude to the game. Shame, because at its core its not too bad.

Progressive Rating: 8-9-8-7-6.

RATING: 5.9
Based on one extended game session where my pilot did pretty well (2 kills and lived to fight again) I'm not as impressed with this game as I expected to be.

I enjoy Wing of War/Glory as a light war themed game with aircraft shaped counters (it's no war game or flight-sim) and was expecting to find X-Wing somewhat similar but set in the Star Wars Universe, I was disappointed.

To me X-Wing is a puzzle first and a game second, even without using all the pilot and ship extra abilities (cards). For something that's meant to be recreating the lightning-fast action of a cinematic space dogfight there's far too much opportunity for analysis (paralysis) that drags out play time and prevents it from having anything like a 'realistic' feel. The 'hard wired' initiative system only compounds the problem.

There are some very nice ideas (EG the stress system and red/green manoeuvres) but I'll stick to the occasional game of WOW/G and leave X-Wing to the die-hard Star Wars fans and puzzle geeks.

RATING: 9
Really great game.  I'm not a huge Star Wars fan and you don't have to be to enjoy this game.  If you are a fan why haven't you bought this already (don't think, do)?  Great models, good movement system, and expands nicely.

This is not a miniatures game!!!!  If you buy it with this expectation you will be disappointed.  It's a board game that has cool elements of miniature gaming in it, like to scale miniatures, points system, ship customisation, etc.

You will need to buy some expansions as the base game only has two different types of ships and things get stale after a while.  However you don't have to buy loads of expansions either.  I would recommend spending some time deciding which expansions are best for you.

The only issue I have is that it does not scale well to really large games.  You can have huge battles but expect them to take a long time, easily over 5 hours.  Having said that it was designed for smaller ship to ship games and not fielding every model you own (shame, I own lots).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Finally, something to replace Decipher's Star Wars Customizable Card Game as my favorite Star Wars game! Yeah, its only squadron-level dog-fighting, but it feels right. The size difference between the little snub fighters and the capital ships is immense, so a scale integration of the two is not really possible.

Despite the massive amount of components in the Star Wars: X-Wing Miniatures Game - Core Set, the game play is far more intuitive than one would expect. Teaching the game is a very simple affair. Owning the game though is a costly endeavor, as no one is likely to look at the ships included in the Core Set and think, 'Yep, I'm done'. For anyone interested in adding more TIE Fighters and X-Wings to their collection, the Core Set offers the best bang for the buck.

As someone who doesn't have the time or inclination to paint miniatures, the pre-painted ships were a great draw. The models, and their support pillars, are really quite delicate though, so extra care must be taken during play and storage.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

RATING: 8
I never played with SW action figures when I was a kid.  Never got the point, really.  But THIS?  This makes me feel like a 7-year-old again.  Pew, pew!

For the second time at this Gencon, FFG takes an old property (in this case, Wings of War) and gives it a glossy new coat of sci-fi paint.  I'm not too proud to say that as much as I enjoyed Wings of War, this miniatures game is sooooo much better.  Be warned: The 20-minute gameplay is highly addictive, the short rules allow you to play within minutes, and everyone at the table will be talking about Red Leader and speaking into intercoms.

This game could very easily reinvigorate the miniatures market even more than Warhammer 40k and Hordes.  It's a game-changer.

RATING: 9
Absolutely fantastic competitive miniatures skirmish game! Just the right balance of blind luck, calculated risk, tactical acumen, and strategic thinking are required to play this game well. As an added bonus, it also happens to not only be the easiest miniatures game to learn and play that I have ever seen, but the models all come pre-painted (and are rather well-done too!) and are cheaper than you would expect!

If you have not played this game before and you have even a passing interest in miniatures games, you really owe it to yourself to give it a try. You might be surprised at how much you like it!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This game reminds me of many of Avalon-Hill's 1970s-1980s games, in that Fantasy Flight has taken a simple idea--spaceship to spaceship combat with a Star Wars theme--and in its basic version come up with enough rules to put it in the medium-light to medium category of complexity. And that's okay, although it's going to take some time for two or more players to learn this game from scratch. Probably better to get taught by someone who already knows the rules. For example, unlike Milton Bradley's "Star Wars: Epic Duels," which was a game with miniatures, nice bits, and an intuitively easy-to grasp, clean gaming experience, "Star Wars: X-Wing Miniatures Game" strikes me as more an argument for the superiority of video games in this particular context. Its 28-page rulebook, although in color and amply illustrated, is typical of many of the company's rule books--namely, wordy and written in so much detail that it has to be absorbed in multiple readings. However, players can start with the "Quick Play" version, which reduces the game to the basics of setting up, selecting ships and pilots, and moving and fighting. This is useful for learning the basics, and would be good for getting young kids into the game. For adults, however, a quick-play game or two and they've got the basics, and to really enjoy the game as designed, they'll need to jump to warp and start getting all the rules in their heads. To be fair, the 28-page rules book breaks down as follows: 9 pages of regular rules, a 2-page example of play, 2 pages of "additional rules," 3 pages of "advanced rules," and 4 pages devoted to three different "missions." The other 4 pages include a front cover, back cover "quick reference" guide, one page with an "overview" and one other page with a "component guide." And yes, I have played the "Quick Play" version, and yes, I've played with all the regular rules. Except for not having a board, and having to use a ruler to gauge whether one ship's firing field encompasses that of an enemy ship--a feature sure to produce arguments among highly competitive players--the design works. It depends a lot on what level of complexity you're seeking (as well as how much money you care to spend by purchasing the numerous additional ships). Good luck to two newbies trying to break this out of the box and work their way through the regular rules straight out of the box.  On the other hand, although it will take some work, it's not hard to understand. And yet...even though on balance I'd rate it light-medium in complexity, it's curiously fiddly to learn. Purchased new at Target, November 2012.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Not a big fan or miniatures or pre-game element selection type stuff, but this played ok and I enjoyed it enough that I'd play again if someone else who was into it set up the scenario. Eerily similar in concept to Ace Of Aces and Wings Of War et al, as you'd expect, in that you secretly plan your maneuver and speed and then reveal / execute. It has a nice twist in that the best pilots move last and shoot fast, giving a double whammy. So a lot of the game is about guessing, double-guessing and then out-guessing where your opponent will go, aiming to have him in your sights and range after all the moves are done. If you did a normal move (as opposed to a high-stress move), you'll get to do an action, either a bonus mini-move or get a dice-manipulator token. The latter of which helps when you fire, which is a straight dice roll looking for hits, up against a defensive dice roll hoping for evades to cancel the hits. Play 'til things are blown up basically, unless you're playing a mission-type scenario. As such it's pretty clean and I'd say an improvement on the other games mentioned before. But the guts of it is out-guessing, which doesn't hold a lot of interest for me. The attraction is obviously how it brings the theme to life (even if it is at 1/50th normal movie speed) which it succeeds at, but not enough for me to invest.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Played once in late 2013 or early 2014, 6p, one ship each. I liked it!

Oct 2014: Played two 100-point games. I had read that swarms were strong, so I conspired with my nephew on an all Imperial "cheap-ship" squad of 8-tie-fighters. We took on 4 cadillac rebel ships, and lost not a single tie. Obliterated my brother and my other nephew.

We restarted, using the same Imperial TIE squad. My brother shifted to the Falcon and a couple of cheap Rebel fighters, what he could afford for 100 points.

We lost this time, mostly due to a terrible 4th turn when I did not turn my Ties tight enough, and he picked them off one by one with the Falcon. It didn't hurt that the dice didn't cooperate very much, so perhaps a 3rd run same setup might have gone differently.

Either way - I love the game, and there is a place if you can afford it, for this and for ST:Attack Wing But, most people can probably not afford to do both.

Now, with the two new games announced from Fantasty Flight with the Star Wars label (Armada, and some ground-based version), I wonder if this game will fade into the space now holding the Star Wars Miniatures of many gamers, and my brother in particular. I dumped by Star Wars Starship Battles minis for $150 to someone just when X-Wing was being announced back in 2011.

As much as I like this game - I think I'll only be playing my brothers copy until the Next Big Star Wars Property comes out.

Dec 2015: Played a bunch of Armada, love that. However, tasted some games of Epic X-Wing. Ok let's do this. Now fully invested in X-Wing too, bought about 35 ships off eBay for $210, and have since added to it with two epic ships, and several additional Wave 5+ ships, with a big Cool Stuff preorder sitting out there. Have played another 10 games or so, and listened to probably 10 hours of Podcasts. I'm hooked.

May 2016: I have sold hundreds of dollars of my unplayed games, and purchased everything available for this, including duplicates, and epic ships. I also purchased extra copies of core sets and given them to two young guys I have also hooked on the game. I'm working on my 50th play, and only now have passed the obsession point. We were literally playing this 3-4 nights a week for about a month, the most I have played any game in my life. Partially, this was due to having a lot of free time, and partially the two ready opponents who are single and with a lot of free time as well.

However the game is really fantastic, with so much to explore. And so many great podcasts and websites and articles, and a really robust tournament scene (which I will likely never have opportunity to participate in, but it certainly makes for a vibrant game).

July: my buddies have burnt out, didn't make it to Veterans, I'm still super hooked, just spent $92 having HotAC printed deluxe.

April, 2017 - haven't played in a while. SW Destiny now here, and that's taken up my extra game cash. I picked up the custom rebel Tie, the Scum Protectorate fighter, but have skipped most everything else that has come out with wave 10 and 11.

My two regular opponents are now entering their early 20s and work, school, life has them pursuing other interests. My boys don't care for games much anymore either. That leaves my brother, three hundred miles away, and my only opponent. Makes things difficult.

I did give away a starter set to my friend Dave, who has an young son, but is a super geek, if not a gamer. He played a game vs. his wife, which I soured him to buy and AWing and an Interceptor off of amazon, so that's a good sign. He's unlikely to ever be more at best than a once a quarter gamer, probably more like once a year.

So I'm feeling like the arc for XWing is probably over.

RATING: 10
This game is so much fun to play, both the game itself and the metagame.

The game itself has a lot to think about on different levels. You're trying to outguess and outmaneuver your opponent, and thinking through which actions will give your ships the best effectiveness. It does take 5-10 minutes to teach, but it offers a lot of strategic depth. The minis also look amazing on the table and make the whole experience immersive and fun for my inner child who just loves playing with cool toys. :)

The metagame is almost more fun to me. Fantasy Flight does a great job of keeping balance in the ship-building options while constantly adding variety and fixing older ships that didn't quite work. There are lots of different builds that are effective and it's fun to play around with online squad-building tools trying to find a fun and effective combination.

RATING: N/A
I'll take "things I never thought I'd like" for $400, Alex. 

I was never a miniatures gamer, have no interest in them, do not want to paint any miniatures, and ordinarily I have no draw to theme or realism. Neither do I have any interest in hovering over a table making sure my elbows don't inadvertently knock into something while holding a ruler and quibbling about whether or not line of sight is obstructed because I'm a millimeter too far to the left and so can't shoot you. I also have exactly one DNA strand in my body that is sympathetic to science fiction. It is a Star Wars strand (no prequels, please). 

I'm kind of stunned at how simple this game was to learn, but also by how much there was to do, and manage, and have fun with. The game is a simple sequence of making orders, flying a ship, taking actions, fighting, and then resolving. Then you do it again. It all flows really well, it's clean, it's intuitive, and you can mix and match abilities to try and gain little efficiencies for those different points in the sequence. Maybe this game you add some crew to adjust your special actions; next game you choose a different kind of torpedo. It's customizable and variable, and for this Star Wars fan it's a lot of fun. 

Ultimately, I honestly don't even really care if there's a highly strategic game here at all. Right now it's worth the price of admission to play this with my son and chase each other around the dining room table, making laser noises and hunting down one another's best pilots. 

Although [i]what[/i] a price of admission. I have zero interest in the expanded universe ships (what the hell is an E-Wing?) and do not want anything to do with the larger sized models; this fits in one reasonable-sized box in a closet, and that has a lot of value to me. It's a bit annoying how the core set is only three ships, but I picked up a couple extra ships and I'm pretty sure I'm calling it a day with this one. When I was researching this, I watched a few video reviews and some reviewers were already pointing out how some expansion packs were correcting imbalances to make certain ships viable, so I think some Power Creep with this is inevitable. 

I have negative interest in tournaments and have no intention of ever playing this against anyone other than my son and maybe a friend who also knows Star Wars well. I can certainly see how people go down the rabbit hole with this game and end up with 48 TIE fighters and a two-foot-long Tantive IV to escort across a giant table over a two-hour battle, but while I like this game , I don't like it [i]that[/i] much; this is a 30-minute game for me. Any longer and it gets more than a little repetitive, so 2-3 small ships at a time is perfectly OK.

RATING: 6.5
This is such a cool game, specifically the spatial dogfighting. Zooming around the table and dodging each other's firing arcs is a riveting tactical experience.
However, X-Wing is massively bogged down with fiddly design.  Half of play time is spent updating tokens, dealing with clunky positioning rules, and sorting out who can do what and when.
On top of that, actual combat is heavily skewed towards randomness.  The best tactics and god-like dogfighting ability won't save you from unlucky dice rolls.  After a few plays, it begins to feel like it doesn't matter what you field or what you do, who wins is up to fate.

RATING: 4
The people rating this as 10/10 have probably either never played another board game before or are blindly following their Star Wars fanboy-ism.

The game relies VERY heavily on luck (as in, rolling the dice), and even the best strategy you can possibly come up with becomes absolutely useless if you manage to not roll a "hit" or if the opponent manages to evade. Not to mention, most abilities of the crafts and/or the pilots still require you to roll at least a success.

The playmat (which costs a whooping €50) is just a black cloth that doesn't even provide you with a grid to properly place the ships: in fact, you will have to be EXTREMELY careful whenever you want to do anything or you risk altering the positions of the elements on the field. Too many times you will accidentally modify the placement of something with no way of knowing their previous position.

Finally, this game also includes a quite strong element of "pay-to-win" (although it's not the only game that does that, for sure) for many reasons: first, it's IMPOSSIBLE to play a standard match with just the basic set, as the typical fleet strength is 100, which is way higher than the ships included in there; second, in order to create a balanced team you will need to buy additional ships which are also not cheap.

Overall, this is a game I would not recommend even to Star Wars fan, as it is flawed in its fundamentals and there are other similar games that play way better than this, with much less focus on pure luck.

EDIT: Also when touching the X-Wings you have to be EXTREMELY careful, as the laser cannons of the ships from the Force Awakens and the Leagcy set are very fragile.

RATING: 8.225
Simple miniatures dog fight game.  You each select a few ships.  You simultaneously select the flight pattern for that turn (movement of 1-4 inches).  Then you move all the ships and take a shot if anyone is in the attack arc (and range) of your ship(s).  Last ship surviving wins the game.

My 11-year-old daughter and I had a great time playing this game.

It's a good game.  I only have the base set.  I'm not sure that a bunch of different ships would enhance the game that much. but I'm not a Star Wars collector.

RATING: 8.5
Simple enough to play with my six-year-old, but with enough depth to make it interesting for adults.  That's good game design.

Plus, the theme.  Oh, heck, the theme.  The game makes you feel like you're in a desperate shootout with Imperial Lackeys/Rebel Scum.  It's really a perfect marriage of theme to game mechanics.

We've invested in a lot of the expansions, and we just have a blast lining 'em up for dogfights.  Plus, the metagame aspect of building up a force before a game is a lot of fun, and is teaching my kids good stuff.

We've also started playing a campaign game at our FLGS, which has strong RPG elements.  My two boys (5 & 7) love this, and they're enjoying identifying personally with a pilot.

RATING: 8
Components (ie, ships) in this game are FABULOUS! As I've got older, I have less time for painting and want more time for playing - so I've been happy to sacrifice looks in game. Well, x-wing has it all. The ships look very accurate to the movies/books and have an extremely nice pre-paint job. I originally bought the game just for the models alone, as I'd be happy just keeping some for display purposes (what kid of my generation didn't want a Millennium Falcon beside their bed!)

Getting past that, the game mechanics are extremely solid. I appreciate that the individual ships aren't the cheapest - but with a core set and a couple of extra ships, you have all you'd ever need. 

For tournament play, it's a little annoying that some of the best pilot/equipment cards can only be found on ships you might not want to purchase (ie, on the large ships which hold no interest for me) - but that's not going to annoy most players.

The next annoying bit is finding somewhere to play - not everyone has a kitchen table big enough to house the size that the play area should be. But for casual games, making do in a tighter space is fine as both players are similarly limited :)

Overall, I really enjoy x-wing!

RATING: 6.5
We've played a 3-player short introduction game. The scenario was 2 X-Wings versus one Tie-Fighter.

This is a tabletop game where the rules are not so complex. I like the components that help with the navigation of the ships, like curves of different angles. There's luck involved with the dice that determine hits and misses. But I think that good navigation decisions lead to victory, especially when each player controls several space ships. In this case, a good navigator will provoke a situation where he has several space ships simulataniously fireing at a single defending ship. This is a very tactical game.

This base game contains only 3 ships: 1 Tie fighter and 2 X-Wings. I guess there need to be more ships to have a tactically satisfying experience. Maybe it's better to right away buy two boxes instead of one.

RATING: 6
A neat game that is more than just pretty minis.  Compared to Armada, it is faster paced but with more variance.  Each roll and each maneuver has much more randomness, but you will make more of them over the course of the game.  So, it's not necessary high on luck, but individual outcomes can feel that way.  I prefer Armada's more steady pace with more emphasis on planning one really high stakes maneuver well.

While Armada has a few balance problems, they seem small compared to what happens when you play X-wing seriously.  In armada, a couple of price tweaks and everything works well; nothing clumsy, nothing major.

RATING: 9
10-03-2014. I admit, I am not a miniature gaming guy. I admit, I love this game. I must say, I've played mainly scenario 1 repeatedly. 

I like the simplicity of the movement and combat system, after 2 games I've introduced 2 other people to the game and it went over perfectly. The robustness of the game allows you the modify and change stuff on a whim, while keeping a nice balance. Unofficial variants work great (screw 2' x 2').

Games are tense, dice heavy and easy to execute. Hidden movement with dials is very fun, since you need to get into the head of your opponent. Cards with different abilities are provided for and add great flavor to the game. Importantly, (almost) all information you'll need is on the cards/ship to help you memorize/notice your options.

I admit, I think some of the things in this game are a little clunky but I admit the design far outshines my downsides listed here. For example, I think that all the counters are not so interestingly designed and well executed as they could've been (dull!).  I dislike moving the pieces using cardboard rulers and such that allow you to push over the figures. Also, the figures get in the way of maneuvering. I guess these are all small gripes inherent in miniature gaming. As mostly a boardgame enthusiast, I guess a grid would've worked just as well.. I get really annoyed by me pushing over other people's figures the whole time though ;).

All in all. A new favorite game for me.

RATING: 7.5
[color=#CC0000]

I'm a heavy-duty Wings of War player and I find it amusing as hell how long it takes to play single moves in this game.  It's not a problem, because a typical game runs maybe eight moves.  People die quickly in this one.  But as with all things FFG, the simple concept has been deluxified with dozens of special rules in play in each game, likely different every time.  FFG sure knows how to pour chocolate sauce over top of everything.

Enjoyed playing it last night, hope to play again soon.  

As luck would have it I was with a bunch of good guys that didn't care all that much when ships weren't placed exactly right or things got bumped.  I could see how this game could kick off some real fights with people who gave a damn though!

[/color]

RATING: 8
This game is great. Not only has it got great looking components, but the rules are easy to teach as well. Still, it's a game in the 'easy-to-learn-hard-to-master-category' as good tactics will win the game more often than not.

For a miniatures game, this is relatively inexpensive. You can provide two players with enough options for variable army lists for the same amount of money a rulebook and starter army would cost in most miniature game systems. And the miniatures are pre-painted to a very good quality, so this game doesn't need any investments in paints and brushes.

Squad Building gets me back into the vibe of my old LotR-miniature game tournament days.

[b]Also includes:[/b]

Imperial:
8x [thing=123759]TIE Fighter[/thing]
2x [thing=123764]TIE Advanced[/thing]
2x [thing=129431]TIE Interceptor[/thing]

1x [thing=142527]Lambda-class Shuttle[/thing]

RATING: 10
Consider this a rating for the game in general, rather than this specific set.

X-Wing might be the best miniatures game I've ever played. Like all minis games it's clearly a money pit, and it's a difficult game to get into because of that. But the gameplay itself is just about perfect. It's immediately accessible, partially because everyone understands Star Wars, but also because it's fun at its most basic level. It'd be reasonable for someone to buy just a few ships along with the core set, and they will have enough to keep them busy for a while. But FFG is betting that people won't want to stop there, and it's not hard to see why that is. This is a great game.

Its main mechanisms are fine, if sometimes a bit fiddly (this is my only miniatures game - maybe I'm just uninitiated). The combat dice seem to undermine your best-laid plans a bit too often, though many of the cards allow you to augment your results.

RATING: 8
This was fun. Would I have thought this was as much fun if it wasn't Star Wars? Probably not.

I can't get over how expensive this is. You only get three ships with the base game, and they don't even give you enough dice for every pilot's abilities. (Luke can roll 4 attack dice, but they only give you 3.) Of course, you can buy a pack of 6 dice for another $10! Or...what makes the most financial sense is to just buy another base set. So now you're at $60 (if you buy online), and you only have 2 x-wings and 4 tie fighters. Y-wings and advanced tie fighters are blister packs for another $15 retail. The Millenium Falcon will be $30!!

The worst part is that I know my boys would LOVE this game. LOVE IT.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Completely addicted to this game, despite my initial resistance to the "collection creep" of so many expansions. Every time I play is a blast (no pun intended), and collecting all the cool little ships is hugely appealing to the little kid in this 40-year-old body. I think it's a great balance between on the one hand being very playable with nearly any combo of ships you might try in a casual setting, to having all sorts of interesting depth when you're trying to optimize squads for a competitive setting. It's very accessible price-wise, to pick up a Core set and one or two ships that you think look cool, but of course can get expensive if you start to try to be completist or really competitive. In the end, though, I also love that player skill in terms of flying your squads on the table is a huge part of it, and it's not just meta-game analysis and buying special cards to be competitive. Pew pew!

RATING: 8.5
Loving it so far.

2-8-13.  Upgrading this to a 9.0.  Always thinking about this game (at least when work isn't distracting me).  Every time I read about a new build idea, I want to immediately try it out.   This game has legs, it is awesome fun to play, and a nice a mix of skill & luck determine success.  I want to play this until I feel like a master of the system (how I used to feel after playing a MOBA for a long period of time).  I love this game.

4-1-17:  Downgrading just a bit to 8.5  I still think this is a great game, and it's probably the only miniatures game I'll ever play.  I'm dinging it because of set-up and time to play.  I've never been able to finish a full 100-point game in under 2 hours, and it just gets a bit exhausting towards the end.  Maybe it's because I'm slow and my friends are slow, but this is definitely not a 30-45 min game.  I should note that I stopped buying new ships early on and have a very limited collection, which I'm very happy with.  There's too much bloat in the game nowadays, and I don't want to be checking a FAQ every time I play.

RATING: 7
I was drawn to this game due to the style of play. The freeform "board' being a designated play area you move around in, measuring and calculating appealed to me. I am not a major star wars fan, but I do like the movies, so it was worth a go. 

A good friend and I found it extremely fun to play, and immediately after "testing" it out with just the core set, I set forth and got another core set and one of each expansion, which is rare for me to do. 

It's a very interesting game with a lot of re-playability, since no game plays the same twice in a row. Highly recommended.

In the end however, the ever increasing amount of minis that they kept pushing out killed this for me. I just feel utterly abused by FFG at all the pieces they keep trying to get me to buy. In the end, you're into this FAR more then what it's worth.

RATING: 6
I can't picture two adults actually playing this game together without whoever suggested the idea getting embarrassed.  Realising it's a game monkeys can learn they have tried to complicate it with the expanded rules but when you look at these you realise that they are really only canceling each other out, so what is the point of the extra rules.

Lovely quality components, and like my love ww2 planes we all want to love this game...But we all know it's a money making scam that we gladly get sucked into to...overpriced, offers too little for price and keeps expanding...

Top components, improved gameplay etc over wings of war/glory, but like WOW it's just well...

It's a game for kids or one that you play with the kids.

There is so much to like but I just don't think their is a way to make the system work without a radical overhaul.

Although I do think taking the components of this game and using them with my wings of glory planes certainly makes wings of glory more playable.

Playing it with kids it's a high score, maybe 7.  The components are a 10, but the serious game play is about a 3?
But seeing as I play this only with the kids I have rated it appropriately, and am Happy to buy or trade items for this game.

Egyrészt minimális a világról az ismeretem, 1-2 Csillagok háborúja filmet láttam, másrészt a játék a Wreckage-hez hasonló asztalon vonalzóval tologatós játék. A Wreckage-re anno pedig jó szívvel adtam egyes osztályzatot. Szóval nem könnyű. Az alapjáték három hajót tartalmaz, ami nevetségesen kevés pár játék után, szóval muszáj kiegeket vásárolni. Cserében nagyon szépek a miniatűrák, jól kidolgozott az egyes pilóták tulajdonsága, jól kigondolt a harc menete. A legjobban nekem az tetszett, hogy a hajóknak mindig muszáj mozogniuk így mindig érdekes szituációk alakulnak ki, nem fordulhat elő az, hogy x méterről állva lövöldözik egymást. A játék időtartam is jól belőtt. Szóval ég és föld az élmény a Wreckage-hez képest, de azért mégiscsak a vonalzózás a lényeg itt is. Aki Star Wars fanatikus, annak biztosan óriási élmény lehet a játék, de nekem, aki nem is fan és nem is rajong az ilyen típusú játékokért nem igazán "ezzel akarok játszani" játék. Szóval nagyon nehéz pontot meghatároznom. Tessék ezt a fentiek szellemében nézni.

RATING: 8
Something of a guilty pleasure. Not in the sense that the game isn't good, but rather that it's very expensive. I guess you get your moneys worth all the same - the pre-painted ships look fantastic and if you can safely store them and all the associated materials without it taking over your living space, it's worth a look.

Is the game any good? Absolutely. It captures the dogfights of the films extremely well and is fast-paced and exciting with lots to do without getting overly complicated. It also (obviously) looks terrific in play. The only negatives are again the cost of buying the ships and the storage space this will take up. If you can figure something out and you're in any way a Star Wars fan, you need to give this a go.

RATING: 7
Pros:

+ Double-blind action selection is always a win for me (rewards predicting opponent; I feel you should be rewarded for knowing what an opponent is going to do)

+ The game is quick and the dice-rolling is fun

+ Nice to look at

Cons:

-Slippery slope problem once the first ship dies

-I find measuring stuff to be a little clunky and at times ambiguous or subjective, though I understand this is the norm for miniatures games

Neutral:

*Stuff like variable play area size etc. makes the game feels casual for me, which is a fine mindset for this game because it's fun/funny to mess up your moves and crash into stuff and to take risks where you estimate you can ALMOST clear that asteroid or other ship... nope, doh!

* Seemed too simple at first, but that's because I didn't get the maneuvering yet and one of the ships I used was pretty simplistic (YT-1300). By the end of one play I "got" the game though. There aren't many rules/options but the ones that are there efficiently provide a full experience

[b]I'd Rather Play:[/b] Krosmaster Arena

RATING: 6.5
I would rate this game at an ~8 but being a big Star Wars fan since I was 4 years old, I have some personal gripes about the game. First I'll list the immediate Pros and Cons:

Pros: Optional campaign-like missions, well painted minis, easy to learn mechanics, advanced team-building, and tournament level gameplay/events.

Cons: easy to break/very fragile plastic stands and you need to keep an eye on errata updates due to ever-changing meta.

Now for my personal issue with the game:

The mixing of starfighters from Episode 7+ and the Original Trilogy really bothers me. Darth Vader was dead before Kylo Ren and the First Order ever existed, they shouldn't be able to be flown together. If they had separated the two eras into different "sub-games" I would have been okay with it but I understand that there are only a few ships available from the newest trilogy hence why they put them together.

I would have liked to see this game split into three different games with each game representing one of the three different eras depicted in the films [The Clone Wars, Galactic Civil War, and the First Order/Resistance Eras].

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Fun out of box, but I think it could get boring real quick if you're not willing to spend the money to expand your fleet options. That makes this a very expensive game - especially when you realize how much money you've spent and how you need to spend even more to protect it. But if you can afford to buy enough of each ship type to make nearly an entire 100-point fleet out of a each ship type, your options for fleet building really open up.

Single rounds are short (30-60 min), so I think the real fun is going to come in building a fleet, playing it, and then playing it again with a slight variation. The more you learn how various ships/pilot interact, the more fun it will be to try new combinations.

Really looking forward to lots of plays in years to come.

RATING: 8

As time has went on (2 years now) the collection of ships has grown and the game is played more strategically.

Starter set comes with too little dice. Out of the box you need 4 in each colour so why supply 3??

RATING: 10
Faster and more streamlined than wings of war, AND IT'S STAR WARS, what's not to love!

you need two core, three core would be better and the x-wing and tie expansions. the core comes with extra templates, dice and tokens.

all the best pilots are in the expansion packs Wedge, Backstabber and Howlrunner, so they are must haves.

The game hinges on 100 point battles
three core and the expansions will give you 4 x-wings,
a worthy x-wing squad.
but more importantly you will have 7 tie fighters one of the best squads in the game.

later on add the falcon, slave 1 a single tie advanced (for Vader)

later still add in 1 interceptor,and 2-3 b-wings(B-wings are incredible)

The interceptor aces pack is out so buy two of those then you can have 5 interceptors.

tie bombers are cool, but I have yet to make them work, (I have 3)

y-wings are fun, but not necessary. I own 3.
a-wings look cool but more often than not waste points. I have 4.
unless you want the cards, don't buy the shuttle, it is awful. I have 3.

The moldy crow-hawk290 puts too much of a target on it's back to be a viable option, but the cards are nice.

first tournament:
first decide which side you want to play, rebels or empire.

next, how many ships will you be comfortable flying in the set amount of time?

Tournament rounds are usually 75 minutes, if the time is less than that, I recommend not taking a swarm (6 or more ships).

how many different dials are you going to be able to fly at once, different dials can cause confusion.

for rebels I recommend keeping it simple. 

Two Falcons,
one falcon
----- and 2 x-wings,
----- and 2 b-wings,
----- and one x and one B
4x
2x and 2b
2x and 2y
3b and 2a

all the above lists are highly competitive, it depends on your piloting skill and upgrades on how well they work.

The rebel side has a little more hitting power and in the current state (meta) are a little better.

for imperials, more ships is usually better.

6-7 ties
5 ties and vader
4 ties and 2 advanced
2 firesprays with HLC
one firespray and 3 or 4 ties

or if you want to run something hard

one or two shuttles plus bombers.

above all have fun, sit down between rounds, drink plenty of water, eat.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
X-Wing was smoother than I thought it would be. I like that they've taken steps to balance out crafts and crew so that you can play with 2 ships/fleets and have some impression that they are equal. But beyond that, there's nothing here to make me want to pick this up over Wings of Glory; this is more cumbersome and has more rules.

It's perfectly fine, but it's just a shame that FFG feels the current need to remake everything with a Star Wars licence.

Update: Just over a year later and I've gotten into X-Wing in a big way. My own personal way in was through the fan made Arturi Cluster which made the game co-op (against an AI). Whereas usually FFG games like this are intended for a player to build an army or deck and take it to a tournament, Arturi allowed players to work together and so the large combos and overpowered chains are for all players' benefit, making the game much more accessible and appealing.

From there I've developed a taste for building squads and the depth of the game has slowly revealed itself. And what a wonderful game it is. It has some serious luck elements in it and a lot of the game is about managing and mitigating that luck. Suddenly the meta is interesting for the first time for me.

Rating up from 7 to 9.

RATING: 9
The old-school X-Wing and TIE Fighter computer games are some of my favorites of all time.  While this doesn't capture *every* element of the game (I'm probably going to design my own shield deflector/redirection mechanic) it really does bring back so many memories of my youth. It's a lot more tactical than Battleship Galaxies (and I sometimes use pieces from it as NPCs when playing this) but there's some strategy involved when playing missions that aren't just "blow the other guy up."

RATING: 10
 It requires a bit of an investment, but it's incredibly fun as a hobby.  The game-play itself is a great mix of strategy, tactics, skill, and luck.  It's fast-paced, with basically no down-time from start to finish, which makes playing a match super absorbing.  I've been really enjoying it as a hobby, as the organized play community is thriving, and what could be better than hanging out drinking beer and playing X-Wing?

 The squad-building aspect is another layer that adds lots of replayability to the game, as there are basically endless viable configurations of ships, pilots, and upgrade cards to experiment with.  There's so much variety, that everyone can have a different approach to the game, and Fantasy Flight has done a nice job of steadily releasing new ships, while keeping the meta in balance and fairly diverse.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
The games always devolve into ships just running into each other and moving around each other blindly, and victory comes down to pure luck of the dice. Watching some of the tournament games online confirms that this even happens with more experienced players. The luck of the dice can't really be mitigated, so it's not uncommon to roll four or five dice to try to get that last hit on your opponent, then watch as you roll poorly and they avoid any damage.
This has to do with the even dice distribution. You're as likely to roll a hit as your opponent is to roll an evade. I like the Summoner Wars approach better where the attacker is more likely to roll a success, so it keeps the game length down and those big dice rolls are more reliable. The game also drags on for way too long because of this. I haven't actually finished a full game because we usually call it quits after just one or two ships get destroyed and well over an hour has passed.

All of that aside, I like a couple of things about the game. The variety, especially with a few expansions, is really high. For each ship, you've got several different pilots who all work a little differently, plus lots of different upgrades to choose from each game. Another big selling point is the simplicity, once you get past a few fiddly rules involving ship collision and obstacles. You just program your moves, move your ships, attack, and repeat. 

Sold.

RATING: 8.5
Base Game: 8.
(Unofficial) Coop Mode: 9.
Average: 8.5.

Amazing theme, great basic gameplay, great toy factor, amazing variability and replayability. A game that rewards skill despite having a ton of different customizations available. Practice does make you better, there are very few games that actually do this. FUN!

So, what do I not like in the base game? One, the game comes in many small piecies. I don't mind the prices, but hunting for specific expansions to get what you want is not something I particularly enjoy. Two, it's a PvP miniatures game, which requires some commitment to the game from all players, and that reduces the ease of introduction quite a lot.

The custom coop mode of X-Wing is worthy of further notice. Heroes of the Aturi Cluster succesfully turns X-Wing from a PvP to a Coop, which is an amazing feat. Some aspects really need some reworking (level up system and player ship balance) but others like mission design, scaling and campaign design are spectacular. It's a 0.7 version as of Feb2016, so that explains it, but overall it's already an amazing system.

As a side note, I would recommend Scum as your first faction as the upgrades used in most good scum lists are relatively self-contained in Scum expansions as opposed to Rebels or Imperials, whose sought upgrades are strewn throughout many a faction.

RATING: 6
I'm a wargamer and I own a lot of this. The base game is an excellent theme with excellent fundamental mechanics. A great movement system with exciting choices. Really delivers the feeling of flying in a dogfight.

Expansion bloat, combined with the combo nature of FFG's upgrade system makes this game difficult to understand and fundamentally less enjoyable. The presence of turrets  (ships that shoot 360 degrees) heavily mitigate the reward for skilful flying and thus the charm of the game.  The number of component's in this game effectively makes this a 90-120 time commitment for what feels like it should be a 45 minute game.

Great system badly in need of a reboot and some simplification.

RATING: 10
