=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Absolutely brilliant game. The game that got me into a genre I didn't think I'd ever enjoy; miniatures games (I tried warhammer 40k and hated everything about it). At it's heart x-wing was simple, elegant and had a surprising amount of tactical depth. 

It's a shame that the tournament version of the game has shaped the game as a whole as simple dogfights are by far the most boring way of playing the game. I think FFG have released too many pointless new ships and cards. It's become over-complicated and fiddly. A lot of the rules are on cards and FAQs. I had a look at the latest FAQ and it shows what a bloated monster the game has become. They've turned a lithe Han Solo of a game into a corpulent Jabba the Hutt! The simple order of a turn has been split into sub phases. It's all a master class in his to ruin a game through unnecessary tinkering. Thankfully the bloat can all be ignored and the game enjoyed in its original form in so-called 'casual' play. I think it would be good if FFG released more scenarios and campaigns and fewer ships and cards.

I still enjoy flying the classic Star Wars fighters against each other, and missions are really good way to enjoy the tactical positioning aspects of the game. I'll have to try out Heroes of the Aturi Cluster for a co-op campaign game soon.

RATING: 9
Simple but with hidden depths (a bit like me..) this skirmish-cum-strategy minis game has a lot of potential. Absolutely requires the right blend of forces (and the TIEs seem a bit overpowered using just the core set) but a fine start to what I hope to be a long-running series.
Revision, 09/02/15: With expansions, the game opens up into something quite spectacular. I've updated the score from 7 (core game) to 9 (core game + expansions) as mechanically it's good anyway, but the expansions not only add buffs and models, they also improve the mechanics (large ship sizes, Modifications, Boosts, Ion rule tweaks, cloaking... the list is almost endless). An indispensable game!

RATING: 6
The game system is a 6, the miniatures make it a 7!
... but beware of collectible nature of it, it gets expensive fast.

[+] game system is easy, gameplay is smooth, squadron building can be fun (with enough expensions to choose from), miniatures are gorgeous, love the theme
[-] must buy expensions to make it worth, expensive! 

Note: there is a point where 1 squadron is doomed, game should end there (at players discretion) and never drag on till the last ship is down.

UP: I recently discovered the co-op/solo campaign "Heroes of the Aturi Cluster" (developped by fans), it has rules for AI imperial ships that are pretty smart. The campaign requires a lot of ships to be enjoyed entirely, but with few ships you can still play a few scenarios. There's a lot to print & assemble for full effect, it's obvious that a lot of work was put into that and it seem to work well. There's an experience system and "levelling" up your pilot between missions, very cool overall, I recommand checking it up (download available from FFG)

Would this be as good and re-playable without expansions? Maybe not, but is this something you'd ever want to not keep growing?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Okay, long comment because I think this is a really good game but I want to clearly explain why I don't rate it higher. The game pretty much feels like this to me: spend 10 mins maneuvering. Either I've outmaneuvered my opponent (yes!) or I've been outmaneuvered (no!). At which point a perfectly-lined-up perfectly-timed shot is taken....which probably does nothing. Or even if it does something, it might remove a damage or a hull point, which is pretty much nothing.

10 more mins of maneuver for the same result.

Then 10 more mins of maneuver for the same result.

Etc.

OR

Everyone flies into a big cluster in the middle, people crash/collide, fire is concentrated, etc. and tons of stuff dies. Now either one player has an overwhelming advantage so the game might as well be over, or both players have just a small force left so begin the 10-mins-of-maneuver-for-that-one-perfectly-timed-shot cycle and repeat for the next hour.

So that's the part that just isn't my cup of tea. I totally get that many people would love the constant maneuvering, and I'm happy they love the game. But I think maybe my background of chess and Warhammer Fantasy has me disliking that. In both of those games, maneuvering happens at the beginning. You arrive at a position that you have carefully planned and worked for, and then the crap hits the fan and you find out which player's ideas were stronger and more well-thought-out. With X-Wing it feels like the planning and maneuvering is often pointless because outmaneuvering an opponent several times a game only to come up empty on the dice was pretty common. And I LOVE dice. I love randomness and chance in my games, just not the way it comes out in X-Wing. Also, how many times in the movies does a pilot outmaneuver another pilot, get behind him, get off that perfect shot, and then not destroy the enemy fighter? It seemed not only anti-climactic but anti-thematic as well. Still a beautiful game though, without a doubt.

Possibly this could all be solved by somehow eliminating defense dice.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
French
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Very very boring game. Similar to Wings of Glory, but simpler and less satisfying. Wings of Glory languishes down at 500-something in the BGG rankings and this doesn't... Because Star Wars.

Star Wars are great popcorn films, but they don't compete with the First and Second World Wars, which were tragic, moving and important. Go read some history and play something that celebrates the courage of people who fought, suffered and died in their millions fighting Hitler. 

Other problems with this game compared to Wings of Glory. In Wings of Glory, you can buy four planes and have a good game. Star Wars X-Wing is a license to print money by FFG. I played the core set with three ships and it's not a complete game. You have to buy other ships, which no one else seems to mind. Because Star Wars.

It's too luck-based with the dice rolling so, even when you get near the other ships, you'll probably miss. Oh yes, and for what is basically a casual skirmish game, X-Wing has FAR too much deckbuilding. Before you can miss a shot, you'll be choosing pilots, ships, blah blah. This is because the game supports a tournament scene, which Wings of Glory doesn't. Because Star Wars.

If you're considering this game and aren't a Star Wars fan, I'd recommend picking up four planes for Wings of Glory. It's cheaper, the planes look really nice, and you can teach your kids some history. The difficulty of Wings can be customised too - you can play as an easy skirmish, or you can add pilots, height changes, etc. Even better, there's no dice rolling so the game ends quickly. Get into firing range of another plane and they take a random damage counter. Destroy two of four planes and the game ends.

RATING: N/A
An elegant little dogfighting game that's evolved (by FFG's 'living card/minis game' model) into something a little more top-heavy. Competitive play is very pricey, but $100 buys a core set and a handful of expansions -- enough to give you months of superb tactical minis combat. It's unquestionably worth it: between the exquisite core design and the bliss of flying iconic Star Wars ships ('pew pew pew!!' sounds not included), X-WING is a stone classic. Enthusiastically, unreservedly recommended to anyone who ever dreamt of beating Han Solo's time on the Kessel Run.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I do have many additional ships for the game, but there really is no need to list them all here.

Here's the deal: this game is excellent.  It is tactical, fun, exciting and challenging.  If you are a Star Wars fan, it is a no-brainer.  The one thing that scared me off of this game for years was that I thought it was going to be a money sink.  If you are going to play casually, it definitely does NOT have to be a game that you drop a lot of cash into.  It is visually beautiful and worth checking out.  

EDIT (February, 2017): I wrote the above comments prior to getting involved in the competitive scene, and I do believe those comments still hold true.  I didn't like the competitive aspect as much as I thought I would, but I still love this game and will happily join in on a tournament once in a while.

RATING: 7.5
I think X-Wing is a great "lite" skirmish game.  The game moves quickly and stays tense thanks to the way players lock-in ship movements in secret, creating a delightful second-guessing element.  The dice do just the right thing here: creating tension but not being so random as to completely spoil good strategy.

The squad-building is where the game really shines, opening up customization and many additional features and tactics.

I enjoy that the game is superbly simple to teach, quick and exciting to play, yet manages to offer variety and depth enough that will keep it fresh for a long time.

Oh...and the models are incredibly gorgeous...

RATING: 5.5
[i]X-Wing Miniatures[/i] improves on the Wings of War system in places, but every positive change seems to be balanced out by a negative.

Why X-Wing is better than WoW: cardboard movement templates, a theme that many gamers know and love, an updated critical hit system, it's fun to roll dice.

Why X-Wing is worse than WoW: insta-death (= bad die rolls), player downtime in large battles, an underwhelming base set, price point.

It was easy to remedy the instant kill in WoW, since all you had to do was remove the pilot death card.  There's no such option in X-Wing, since dice govern all damage.  So after 20-40 minutes of set-up players can be knocked out immediately if they don't roll well on defense.  That sucks, especially when there are 90 minutes remaining in the game for everyone else.

The initiative system adds flavor and strategy to the gameplay, but it also adds a ton of downtime when more than a few players are involved.  That's enough to kill my interest in X-Wing right there.

Lastly, to hammer on the value issue, X-Wing is WAY overpriced given that no one in their right mind would be content with the pitiful number of models included in the base set.  So fans of the game are dropping $75+ if they're dropping anything at all.  That's acceptable for obsessive fans and most miniatures gamers, but anyone who doesn't fall into either category (like me) is bound to flinch.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.8
I don't know if it's mostly because of the theme but I enjoyed this much more than Wings of War. 

The movement is handled well by the dial, and I liked the red/green mechanism. The combat dice are cool too since there are a couple layers to it. 

The action system is nice but we took focus 90% of the time which led to a good amount of null combat. I don't think this is a flaw in the system as much as me not using the locking action as an X-wing. So I think I'd just have to play a bit more and determine the situational use of each.

We did have a bit of circling for a while, with a lot of misses/evades due to the focus action. Like I said, it's probably because we're both relatively new to the game but I'd like it more if it sped up a bit. I'd also like to see a fight with a few different units on each side but that would get expensive very quickly.

RATING: 7.5
I have played this game a few times now and it's a blast to play. Having a squadron of ships at your command and the tactical nature of the gameplay is very enjoyable. The game itself is very easy to understand and isn't overly rules-complex. It also looks amazing when you have it all set up...

The only real knock that I have against it is the fact that you really do need to buy quite a few ships to make it worth your while. At one time I thought that I'd like to get at least two of all the ships but have since settled on getting one of all of the original trilogy ships instead.

For something that's as entertaining as this is, it really should get to the table more than it has. The last time I played my set was at the end of 2013, and the last time I played it at all was at GenCon 2014. It would be nice to break this out sometime soon.

RATING: 8
Nice variation of Wings of War. Real selling points are original(and expanded) Star Wars universe, really great looking ships (the pre-painted miniatures are top-notch). FFG captured the magic of original SW. I might like more the non-dice approach of WoW, but all the stuff that X-Wing adds feel really appropriate to Star Wars feel. I can't really complain.

Huge ships finally snapped my spine and I started to collect this game.

edit: I'm probably not going to buy anything from Scum & Villainy faction. Its introduction left me cold. The magic of x-wing for me is the rebel vs imperium conflict. I'm hoping that they will release more huge ships in the future.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
After a couple of years cautiously observing from a safe distance, we finally took the plunge and grabbed a starter box plus a few extra ships. Haven't played it much yet. Not sure whether it will grab us or not. 

Prepainted miniatures games like X-Wing suffer from 'neither one thing nor t'other' as far as I'm concerned. They're too expensive compared to boardgames (because you don't get everything you need in one box), yet they're not as rewarding as 'proper' miniatures games (for which painting, making scenery, etc., forms a large part of the enjoyment). Still, we'll see...

RATING: 8.5
Movement and manoeuvres is really something in this one. In my first big game I crashed into my own ships very often and could not hold formation. I need a lot more practice. There is a lot of luck from the dies but it mitigates over the course of a game. The ships don't go down easily, there's a lot of attrition battling going on. This could be due to our inexperience though. 

It's very fun to field different squads and to test out different strategies. Overall I think this is a great game. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I love this game. It isa great 2-player, semi-casual game of tactics and dog fighting, with the coolest space theme out there for ships shooting ships. I play this with a few friends, and they all love it, and a few opponents is all i need to continue enjoying this. I used to play MtG, and this satisfies my collection disorder, and allows for others to play my collection, which is more manageable, and affordable than an MtG collection.

RATING: 7.5
Rating used to be much higher... until I got sick of it.

Dogfighting gets old rather quickly (to me), new expansions only brings up new permutations to rather a convoluted system as it stands right now, lack of faction identity, reliance on luck (or mitigation) spoils the competitive scene and due to its popularity the community grew a bit toxic.

RATING: 8.2
如果你还在为模型兵棋高昂的价格望而却步，如果你还在为自己拙劣的涂装技巧感到懊恼，如果你还在为场地、规则、玩伴诸多种种受到限制，那么可以考虑体验一下X翼战机这款模型兵器游戏。有简单直观的遭遇战标准竞技模式，也有模拟剧情完成特定任务模式。基础核心游戏投入不大，，即便不喜欢，也不必为这些投少少投入感到可惜，但却可以从中一窥模型兵棋的神秘。如果喜欢上了，后续的扩充包采购也非常灵活，但是有一点是必须的，一个同样爱好这个系列的桌友玩伴。
【关键词】飞船四维数值，行动轮盘，行动导轨，射程标尺，飞行员技能值，联队分值，陨石障碍，星球大战背景，任务模式，攻防八面骰，模型

【推荐度】中【模型兵棋推演，轻中度模型战棋爱好者
